<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="main-objective">Main objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The student will acquire knowledge, skills, and attitudes to promote health, prevent illness, diagnose, manage and rehabilitate infants and children suffering from common childhood conditions/diseases</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="course-outline">COURSE OUTLINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#course-outline" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Identify children with normal growth and development.</p>
<ul>
<li>Recognize and manage deviation from normal growth patterns</li>
<li>Triage and provide emergency care to infant and children</li>

<li>Apply I.M.C.I. knowledge in managing children under five years</li>
</ul>

<p>3</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="growth-and-development">Growth and development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#growth-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>All body systems undergo progressive maturation; concurrent development of skills allows infants to increasingly respond to the environment. Acquisition of these fine and gross motor skills occurs in an orderly head to toe and center to periphery sequence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="proportional-changes">Proportional changes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#proportional-changes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Growth is rapid during the first year, especially the initial 6 months. Height increases by 2.5 per month during the first 6 months. Increase in length occur, sudden spurts rather than in a slow, gradual pattern. Average height is 65cm at 6 months and 74cm at 12 months. By 1 year the length has increased by almost 50%. This occurs mainly in the trunk rather than the legs and contributes to the characteristic physique of the older infants.</p>
<p>Head growth is rapid and an important determinant of brain growth. Head circumference increases approximately 2 cm per month from birth to 3 months, 1 cm per month from 4 to 6 months. The average head size is 43 cm at 6 months and 46 cm at 12 months. By 1 year, the head size has increased by almost 33%.</p>
<p>Closure of cranial sutures occurs, with the posterior fontanelle fusing at 6 to 8 weeks and the anterior fontanelle closing by 12 to 18 months of age.</p>
<p>It is important to note that genetic, metabolic, environments and nutritional factors strongly influence infant growth. Use appropriate growth charts reflecting weight for length and head circumference in each case to determine appropriate growth parameters. Expanding head size reflects the growth and differentiation of the nervous system.</p>
<p>The chest assumes a more adult contour, with the lateral diameter becoming larger than the anterioposterior diameter. The heart grows less rapidly than the rest of the body does; its weight is usually doubled by 1 year of age, where as the body weight triples over the same period.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="milestones">Milestones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#milestones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A child's development represents the interaction of heredity and the environment on the developing brain. Heredity determines the potential of the child, while the environment has to meet the child's physical and psychological needs. These vary with age and stage of development;</p>
<ul>
<li>An infant is totally physically dependent on his parents and requires a limited number of cares to meet his psychological needs.</li>
<li>A primary school-age child can usually meet some of his physical needs and cope many social relationships.</li>
<li>Teenagers are able to meet most of their physical of their physical needs while experiencing increasing increasingly complex emotional needs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="four-areas-of-development">Four areas of development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#four-areas-of-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Gross motor</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fine motor and vision</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Speech, language and hearing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social, emotional, behavior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gross motor</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>In the first 18 months of life there is rapid motor development from an immobile newborn infant to one who is able to adopt an upright posture.</p>
<ul>
<li>Acquisition of tone and head control
By 6 weeks an infant can lift his head and move it from side to side. By 3-4 months of age the infant can hold his head upright when held sitting.</li>
<li>Primitive reflexes e.g. Moro, grasping etc. need to disappear by to allow motor development to progress, and almost all do so by 4-6 months of age.</li>
<li>By 6 months an infant will sit without support</li>
<li>Locomotor pattern
He becomes mobile, with crawling at 8-9 months of age, walks around furniture at 10 months, and take his first steps unsupported at 12 months, some can walk unsteadily, with broad gait and hands apart. At 20 months can kick a ball, hop on one leg, go up and down stairs, one leg at a time, jump and pedal a bicycle.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-fine-motor-and-vision">2. Fine motor and vision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-fine-motor-and-vision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fixing, following and visual alertness
By six weeks the infant will be visually alert and when supine will move his head from side to side to follow an object.</li>
<li>Hand regard
At 3-4 months, infants show hand regard, spending a lot of time looking at their hands.</li>
<li>Grasp reflex, voluntary grasping, pincer grasp, pointing:
A new born will grasp an object and at six months the infant is able to grasp actively with the whole hand (palmar grasp). Has a good pincer grip (thumb and first or second finger) of a small object at 10 months of age. Soon afterwards the infant points at objects with the index finger.</li>
<li>Handling objects with both hands and transferring: At 6 month’s infants should be able to handle objects with both hands and transfer objects from one hand to another. There should be no hand dominance during the first year.</li>
<li>Manipulation of small objects, writing, building bricks, dressing. At 14 months children are able to grip when they hold the pencil and their ability with building blocks, and they are able to scribble. Subsequent skills are dressing, writing, and key board skills.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-speech-and-language-and-learning">3. Speech and language and learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-speech-and-language-and-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sound recognition and vocalization: The newborn infant stills to voice and startles to loud noises. He responds to his mother’s voice at 6 weeks of age even when she cannot be seen. Vocalization emerges and by 4 months the infant is making vowel sounds.</li>
<li>Cools and babes: At 6 months babies start to use monosyllables e.g. 'ba' 'da'. At 7-8 months they turn to voice and acquire two syllables like 'dada' 'mama' none specifically.</li>
<li>Single words and understanding simple requests: Appropriate use of single words such as ‘dada’ or ‘mama’ and one or two words occurs at 13 months and also understanding simple commands such as ‘no’ or ‘give’ me and respond to their names. By 18 months children can say can say about ten words and can demonstrate six parts of the body</li>
<li>Joining words, phrases: At 18 months he can combine two words and at 24 months he can combine three words.</li>
<li>Simple and complex conversation: Between 2-3 years the conversation becomes increasingly complex with phrases followed by sentences. At 3 years knows his age and a few colours.</li>
</ul>
<p>4</p>
<p>5</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-social-and-emotional-behavior">4. Social and emotional behavior<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-social-and-emotional-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Smiling, social responsiveness: Smiling at 6 weeks is an important and remarkable constant milestone. It means that the baby smiles in response to someone smiling directly at him. At 10 months they will wave ‘bye bye’ if they wish to.</li>
<li>Separation anxiety: At about 18 months of age, many infants become anxious and unhappy when separated from their mother or care taker and become aware of strangers.</li>
<li>Self help skills, feeding, and dressing: infants will put solid food into their mouth at about 6 months of age, drink from a cup by 12 months and hold a spoon and feed themselves safely at 18 months. At 24 months infants are able to remove garments.</li>
<li>Symbolic play: At 24 month’s children symbolic play where they play with toys such as doll, brush, chair, spoon and they play as if they were life size equivalents.</li>
<li>Social behavior: Once mobile children explore the surrounding and require constant attention and supervision. Problems may arise with food refusal, reluctance to go to sleep, waking up at night, temper tantrums and antisocial behavior. During the second year of life children play on their own or alongside others (parallel play) and only subsequently learn interactive play at three years plus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a94647c2">Erikson’s theory of psychosocial development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a94647c2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Erikson’s theory of psychosocial development has eight distinct stages and he assumes that a crisis occurs at each stage of development. Successful completion of each stage results in a healthy personality and the acquisition of basic virtue whereas failure to successfully complete a stage can result in a reduced ability to complete further stages and therefore a more unhealthy personality and sense of self.</li>
</ul>
<p>The different ages and stages relevant to paediatric nursing (Erik Erickson)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Stage</th><th>Psychosocial crisis</th><th>Age</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>Trust vs. mistrust</td><td>Infancy(0 to 1 1/2)</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Autonomy vs. shame</td><td>Early childhood (1 ½ to 3)</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Initiative vs. guilt</td><td>Play age (3 to 5)</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Industry vs. Inferiority</td><td>School age (5 to 12)</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Ego identity vs. Role confusion</td><td>Adolescence (12 to 18)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-trust-vs-mistrust">1. Trust vs. Mistrust<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-trust-vs-mistrust" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During this stage the infant is uncertain about the world in which they live and infant looks towards their primary caregiver for stability and consistency of care. Infants will develop a sense of trust if they receive consistent, predictable and reliable care. Success in this stage will lead to the virtue of <strong>hope</strong> Failing to acquire the virtue of hope will lead to the development of fear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-autonomy-vs-shame-and-doubt">2. Autonomy vs. Shame and Doubt<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-autonomy-vs-shame-and-doubt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At this stage the child is mobile and developing physically children begin to assert their independence by walking away from their mother, picking which toy to play with discovering that he or she has many skills and abilities, Such skills illustrate the child's growing sense of independence and autonomy. Children should be allowed to explore the limits of their abilities within an encouraging environment which is tolerant of failure. Parents must try not to do everything for the child but if the child fails at a particular task they must not criticize the child for failures and accidents (particularly when toilet training). The aim has to be “self-control without a loss of self-esteem”. Success in this stage will lead to the virtue of <strong>will</strong>.</p>
<p>6</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Initiative vs. Guilt</li>
</ol>
<p>During this period the primary feature involves the child regularly interacting with other children at school. Central to this stage is play, as it provides children with the opportunity to explore their interpersonal skills through initiating activities.</p>
<p>Children begin to plan activities, make up games, and initiate activities with others. If given this opportunity, children develop a sense of initiative, and feel secure in their ability to lead others and make decisions.</p>
<p>Conversely, if this tendency is marred, either through criticism or control, children develop a sense of guilt. They may feel like a nuisance to others and will therefore remain followers, lacking in self-initiative.</p>
<p>The child takes initiatives which the parents will often try to stop in order to protect the child. The child will often overstep the mark in his forcefulness and the danger is that the parents will tend to punish the child and restrict his initiatives too much.</p>
<p>It is at this stage that the child will begin to ask many questions as his thirst for knowledge grows. If the parents treat the child’s questions as trivial, a nuisance or embarrassing or other aspects of their behavior as threatening then the child may have feelings of guilt for “being a nuisance”.</p>
<p>Too much guilt can make the child slow to interact with others and may inhibit their creativity. Some guilt is, of course, necessary, otherwise the child would not know how to exercise self control or have a conscience.</p>
<p>A healthy balance between initiative and guilt is important. Success in this stage will lead to the virtue of purpose.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Industry (competence) vs. Inferiority</li>
</ol>
<p>Children are at this stage will be learning to read and write, to do sums, to do things on their own.</p>
<p>The child’s peer group will gain greater significance and will become a major source of the child’s self-esteem and now feels the need to win approval by demonstrating specific competencies that are valued by society, and begin to develop a sense of pride in their accomplishments.</p>
<p>If children are encouraged and reinforced for their initiative, they begin to feel industrious and feel confident in their ability to achieve goals. If this initiative is not encouraged, if it is restricted by parents or teacher, then the child begins to feel inferior, doubting his own abilities and therefore may not reach his or her potential. Yet again, a balance between competence and modesty is necessary. Success in this stage will lead to the virtue of competence.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Identity vs. Role Confusion</li>
</ol>
<p>This is the transition period from childhood to adulthood. Children are becoming more independent, and begin to look at the future in terms of career, relationships, families, housing, etc. The individual wants to belong to a society and fit in. They learn the roles they will occupy as an adult. It is during this stage that the adolescent will re-examine his identity and try to find out exactly who he or she is.</p>
<p>Erikson claims that the adolescent may feel uncomfortable about their body for a while until they can adapt and “grow into” the changes. Success in this stage will lead to the virtue of fidelity.</p>
<p>Fidelity involves being able to commit one's self to others on the basis of accepting others, even when there may be ideological differences.</p>
<p>During this period, they explore possibilities and begin to form their own identity based upon the outcome of their explorations. Failure to establish a sense of identity within society ("I don't know what I want to be when I grow up") can lead to role confusion. Role confusion involves the individual not being sure about themselves or their place in society.</p>
<p>7</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychosexual-stages-of-development">Psychosexual Stages of Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychosexual-stages-of-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>According to Freud, childhood experiences shape our personalities and behavior as adults.</p>
<p>☐ Oral (0-1 years of age): During this stage, the mouth is the pleasure center for development. Freud believed this is why infants are born with a sucking reflex and desire their mother's breast. If a child's oral needs are not met during infancy, he or she may develop negative habits such as nail biting or thumb sucking to meet this basic need.</p>
<p>☐ Anal (1-3 years of age): During this stage, toddlers and preschool experiment the control they learn to exert over their bodily functions is manifested in toilet-training. Improper resolution of this stage, such as parents' toilet training their children too early, can result in a child who is uptight and overly obsessed with order.</p>
<p>☐ Phallic (3-6 years of age): During this stage, preschoolers take pleasure in their genitals and, according to Freud, begin to struggle with sexual desires toward the opposite sex parent (boys to mothers and girls to fathers). For boys, this is called the Oedipus complex, involving a boy's desire for his mother and his urge to replace his father who is seen as a rival for the mother's attention. At the same time, the boy is afraid his father will punish him for his feelings, so he experiences castration anxiety. The Electra complex, later proposed by Freud involves a girl's desire for her father's attention and wish to take her mother's place.</p>
<p>☐ Latency (6-12 years of age): During this stage, sexual in stint subside, and children begin to further develop the superego, or conscience. Children begin to behave in morally acceptable ways and adopt the values of their parents and other important adults.</p>
<p>☐ Genital (12+ years of age): During this stage, sexual impulses reemerge. If other stages have been successfully met, adolescents engage in appropriate sexual behavior, which may lead to marriage and childbirth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-influencing-growth-development">Factors influencing growth &amp; development:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-growth-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-genetic-factors">1. Genetic factors.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-genetic-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Heredity: Hereditary traits are passed to the offsprings.eg tall parents tend to have tall children. Parents with high intelligence quotient are more likely to have children with high intelligence quotient.</li>
<li>Racial: Different racial groups have varying growth potentials</li>
<li>Gender: Pubertal growth spurt occurs earlier in girls, mean height and weight of girls are usually less as compared to boys of the same age.</li>
<li>Chromosomes: Some chromosomal abnormalities can affect growth and developmwnt.eg Turner or Downs’s syndrome.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-nutritional">2. Nutritional<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-nutritional" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nutritional deficiency considerably retards physical growth. Malnourished mother produce babies with IUGR. Over nutrition may cause obesity. So to control the nutritional requirements of mother is necessary to have a health child. Lack of proper nutrition can interfere with the maturation of your child’s brain and body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-environmental-factors">3. Environmental factors.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-environmental-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Maternal infections: Some diseases passed from mother to fetus can lead to arrest or retard the fetal development.eg syphilis, viral hepatitis, and toxoplasmosis. Maternal rubella can cause congenital malformations in the infant if it occurs during the first trimester.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Exposure to teratogens: abnormal fetal growth and development can be caused by intrauterine exposure to smoking, alcoholism, drug intake and radiation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Infections and infestations: Systemic infections and parasitic infestations can decrease the rate of growth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Systemic disease: chronic conditions whether communicable or non communicable can have adverse effects on growth. Chronic untreated diseases of heart, lungs, liver etc. impair growth and development seriously. Growth Hormone Deficiency, Hypothyroidism, Cushing’s syndrome etc. medical condition that needs early attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hormones and drug: Androgenic hormones and steroids accelerate skeletal growth, however ultimately epiphyses of bones close prematurely and the bone growth ceases relatively earlier.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-high-social-economic">4. High social economic;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-high-social-economic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>High social economic level families have a superior nutritional state; neglect has an adverse affect on development.</li>
<li>Emotional factors: Children from broken homes and orphanages do not grow and develop at an optimal rate. Anxiety, insecurity, lack of emotional support and love, poverty, disturbed parent-child relationship, child abuse among others may adversely affect development.</li>
<li>Cultural factors: Religious taboos and cultural beliefs plus myths of a community can affect the nutritional state and growth performance of children.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-dfded08d.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg">
Deviations from normal growth and development and their management</p>
<p>9</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="variations-in-normal-development">Variations in normal development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#variations-in-normal-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Average</li>
<li>Slow starters, later coming to average.</li>
<li>Advanced in general or in a specific field.</li>
<li>Persistently retarded in all fields, becoming average or advanced</li>
<li>Intermittent gaps in development</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="slow-starters">Slow starters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#slow-starters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Such children are often late in acquiring certain skills such as walking, sphincter control. Sometimes this may be familial tendency. Some children may show retardation in all fields and go on to be normal</p>
<p>In case a child shows gross slowness in a particular field while normal in others, look for the cause. Some causes of isolated motor development variations include familial factors, environmental factors, and personality traits eg. Children of apprehensive mothers who are worried and frightened that something might happen to their children are late learners. A one year old child may refuse to walk due to ill fitting shoes and children with hypotonia (Down’s syndrome, malnutrition, rickets, and hypothyroidism) or hypertonic (cerebral palsy) walk late.</p>
<p>Visual impairment or neuromuscular disease results in delayed motor development. NB At times no cause can be found for a transient delay in a particular field and such children grow up to be normal.</p>
<p>Children with visual handicap, diminished parent child interaction, institutional care, and facial muscle atrophy may smile late or never smile.</p>
<p>Usually a child is dry at 2 years and by night at 3 years; however some might continue to wet their bed up to 5-6 years. This may be due to delayed maturation of CNS or familial. Delay in speech is not always abnormal as it may be attributed to familial factors, poor environment or even mental abnormality and so deafness and autism should be ruled out.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="children-with-temporary-developmental-gaps">Children with temporary developmental gaps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#children-with-temporary-developmental-gaps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Temporary developmental gaps may be witnessed in normal children who have suffered illness eg. Encephalitis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="progressive-slowing-and-retardation-in-all-fields">Progressive slowing and retardation in all fields<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#progressive-slowing-and-retardation-in-all-fields" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Progressive slowing and retardation in all fields is almost always pathological, children who manifest with a continuous deterioration in their development have one or other degenerative disorders</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advanced-development">Advanced development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advanced-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Children who grow up to have higher than average IQ may show indication of this in childhood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-physical-growth">Disorders of physical growth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-physical-growth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Physical growth is measured in terms of weight and height.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="failure-to-thrive">Failure to thrive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#failure-to-thrive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def; Failure to thrive has no universal definition. Failure to thrive is a term assigned to a child whose weight for age is below <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>3</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3^{\mathrm{rd}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">3</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">rd</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> percentile or a downward change in growth that has crossed two major growth percentiles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Inadequate calorie intake e.g. incorrect formula, poverty</p>
<p>Inadequate absorption e.g. cystic fibrosis, celiac diseases</p>
<p>Increased metabolism e.g. hyperthyroidism, congenital heart disease, chronic immunodeficiency</p>
<p>Defective utilization e.g. in genetic anomaly such as Trisomy 21 or 18, congenital infection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Weight of the child is less than 2SD. Child interacts poorly with his peers and family members, motor activity is slow, speech is delayed and child remains preoccupied in his own.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Goal is to provide sufficient calories to support 'catch up' growth, a rate of growth greater can be expected rate for age. In addition to adding calorie density to feeds add multivitamin, dietary supplementation with high calorie foods and drinks. Any co existing medical condition should be treated.</p>
<p>Provide a positive feeding environment whether in hospital, at the clinic or home. Teach parents' successful feeding strategies, and supporting the child and family are essential components of care. Take daily weight and record all foods taken and record the child's feeding behavior.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obesity">Obesity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obesity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A child is considered obese when there is excess accumulation of fat in the subcutaneous tissue and other parts of the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dietary factors, consuming large infrequent meals</li>
<li>Habits, children speeding more time with in door activities e.g. computer games</li>
<li>Decreased energy expenditure which could be genetically predetermined</li>
<li>Genetic factors, obesity in children has a strong correlation with parental obesity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diet; Reduced calorie intake. These children should be encouraged to reduce sweets and junk food and embrace food rich in fibre and low calorie content.</li>
<li>Encourage physical activity outdoor games and exercise.</li>
<li>Behavior modification; the will of the child to reduce his weight should be strengthened by constant encouragement. Childs weight should be kept under surveillance, restrict television viewing and give psychological support.</li>
<li>Attempts should be made to reduce the weight gradually and a psychologist may be sought to uncover psychogenic causes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="short-stature">Short stature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#short-stature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Short stature is defined as height less than 2 SD (standard deviation) below the mean or and there are two types, proportionate and disproportionate. Proportionate short stature is more common may occur, secondary to constitutional delay in growth, chronic infections, malabsorption, congenital heart disease, congenital heart disease, renal failure or endocrine malfunctioning, whereas disproportionate short stature occurs as a result of abnormal skeletal growth either the limbs or the trunk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Short stature children should be reviewed by the pediatrician</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tall-stature">Tall stature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tall-stature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Child with a height of more than 2SD above the mean Short stature are said to be abnormally tall</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hereditary factors, cerebral gigantism, acromegaly and chromosomal abnormality e.g. Klinefelter syndrome.</li>
<li>NB; most of the tall children are normal and their tallness is based on an optimal environment and genetic predisposition.</li>
</ul>
<p>10</p>
<p>11</p>
<p>Microcephaly</p>
<p>A child is labeled as having microcephaly if his head circumference remains less than 3SD the mean for that age</p>
<p>Causes</p>
<p>Genetic or uterine disturbances, which include chromosomal defects, intra uterine infections and exposure to teratogens, once born, insult to the growing brain can be caused by meningitis, malnutrition, hypothermia and asphyxia.</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>There is no specific treatment and nursing care should be directed toward helping parents to adjust to rearing a child with cognitive impairment when this condition is present.</p>
<p>Macrocephaly</p>
<p>Macrocephaly is defined as a head circumference that is more than 2SD above the mean for that age.</p>
<p>Causes</p>
<p>Increased brain size is increased ventricular size (hydrocephalus)</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>There is no specific treatment for macrocephaly, medical care for children with macrocephaly focuses on management of specific symptoms, such as developmental delays and mental retardation and the primary diagnosis responsible for the macrocephaly.</p>
<p>Paediatric conditions</p>
<p>Impact of sickness and admission to child, parents and family
Immediate and long term</p>
<p>Child</p>
<p>Immediate and long term emotional distress to the child, Children below the age of 5 years are more vulnerable to emotional distress form hospitalization.</p>
<p>Anxiety due to lack of understanding and minimal experience with illness, hospitalization and hospital procedures.</p>
<p>A lack of sensory stimulation in the hospital environment produces listlessness, indifference, unhappiness and even appetite changes. When a child’s motor is restricted, anger and hyperactivity may result.</p>
<p>Parents</p>
<p>Parents have anxiety and concern about their child’s health and this contributes to stress to the child. Parents watching children in pain is difficult and some may feel guilty of not bringing these children earlier to hospital. Parents may exhibit other feelings such as denial, anger, depression, and confusion and parents may deny that their child is ill. They may exhibit anger due to lack of control of caring for their child and may be directed to the nursing staff, family members or higher power Depression may occur due to exhaustion, psychological and physiological requirements of spending long hours in hospital caring for the child. Confusion may arise due to dealing with an unfamiliar environment or the loss of parental roles, long separation and increased stress. At</p>
<p>times parents feel helpless when they play a passive role in their child’s care, such as when a medical procedure is required that hurts or traumatizes the child.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="siblings">Siblings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#siblings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sibling may experience jealousy, insecurity, resentment, confusion and anxiety. They may have, understanding why there sibling is ill or getting all the attention and leaving little for them. Due to changes in roles in the family children may feel insecure or anxious and they develop change in behavior or school performance, during this time siblings feel that they caused the illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family">Family<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Whether planned or unplanned hospitalization increases the family’s stress and anxiety level and this affects all the members of the family, family’s normal routines are disrupted and may alter family roles. Parents and siblings have their own reactions to this experience.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Liberal visitation</li>
<li>Rooming-in in hospital policy</li>
<li>Shorter hospital stays minimizes separation anxiety</li>
<li>Play, recreation and educational opportunities provide an outlet to distract children from illness</li>
<li>Parents attempt to understand by becoming informed and understanding the procedures. They deal with fear of uncertainty and attempt to promote a sense of comfort by interacting with hospital staff. They seek reassurance from the care givers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="respiratory-conditions">Respiratory conditions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#respiratory-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="common-cold-coryza">Common cold (coryza)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-cold-coryza" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Commonest infection in children</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causative-organisms">Causative organisms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causative-organisms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Viruses - Rhinovirus, corona virus and RSV (respiratory syncytial virus)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Clear or mucopululent nasal discharge and nasal blockage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Health education to advice parents that colds are self limiting and have no specific curative treatment. Pain and fever may be treated with paracetamol or Ibuprofen. Antibiotics are not of any benefit and secondary bacterial infection is rare. Saline nasal drops every 3-4 hours.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="streptococcal-sore-throat-pharyngitis">Streptococcal sore throat (Pharyngitis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#streptococcal-sore-throat-pharyngitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Sore throat is inflammation of the pharynx and soft palate.</li>
<li>Etiology</li>
<li>Virus about 90%</li>
<li>Bacterial - Streptococcal infections, Group A Beta hemolytic streptococcal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The pharynx and soft palate are inflamed and local lymph nodes are enlarged and tender.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>12</p>
<p>Sore throat, cough, fever, irritability, malaise, nausea, vomiting, and poor appetite</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treat with oral penicillin-Amoxicillin, Amoxicillin with clavunic acid or IM penicillin and dose should be completed, prescribe Erythromycin for children allergic to penicillin.</p>
<p>Analgesics-paracetamol</p>
<p>Cold or warm compresses may bring relief</p>
<p>Warm saline gargles for bigger children offer throat relief</p>
<p>Do not force to eat, however encourage cool liquids</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tonsillitis">Tonsillitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tonsillitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tonsillitis is extensive inflammation of the tonsils, often with a purulent inflammation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causative-organism">Causative organism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causative-organism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Viral infection</p>
<p>Bacterial infection-group A Beta hemolytic streptococci</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sore throat, difficulty in swallowing, fever, nasal congestion, mouth breathing and drying of mucous membranes aggravates pain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Several pairs of tonsils are part of a mass of lymphoid tissue in oropharynx. Tonsillitis inflammation of the palatine tonsils</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diagnosis is by visual inspection and throat culture</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-management">Medical management.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Viral infection will resolve, institute warm saline gargles, antipyretic.</p>
<p>Bacterial infections-Give penicillin/cefuroxime</p>
<p>Tonsillectomy with or without adenoidectomy can be done under the following conditions</p>
<ul>
<li>Recurrent streptococcal infection</li>
<li>Enlarged tonsils affecting breathing/eating</li>
<li>The child should be 3 years or older</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care">Nursing care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nursing care for children with tonsillitis includes proving comfort; provide a soft diet, warm salt water gargles, throat lozenges, and analgesics/antipyretics.</p>
<p>If surgery is needed- provide psychological preparation, take history which include; bleeding tendency because the operation site is highly vascular, take baseline vitals, blood test for clotting time and check on loose teeth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-operative">Post operative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-operative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Post surgery- until they are fully awake, children should be placed on the abdomen or side to facilitate drainage of secretions, suctioning is performed carefully to avoid trauma on the operated site.</p>
<p>When alert, children may prefer sitting up, however they should remain in bed for the rest of the day.</p>
<p>Discourage from coughing frequently; cleaning their nose or any activity which would injure the operated site, inspect all secretions and vomitus for evidence of fresh bleeding.</p>
<p>Apply ice collar</p>
<p>Give analgesics</p>
<p>Give antiemetic.</p>
<p>Food and fluids are restricted until children are fully alert and with no signs of hemorrhage-cool water, crushed ice and diluted juice is given, however avoid giving fluids with a red or brown color so as to distinguish fresh and old blood in emesis from ingested liquid.</p>
<p>Straws should be avoided since they can damage the surgical site and cause bleeding</p>
<p>Citrus juice may cause discomfort and is usually poorly tolerated.</p>
<p>Milk, ice cream or pudding is not usually offered until clear fluids are retained because milk products coat the mouth and throat, causing the child clear the throat which may initiate bleeding</p>
<p>Children often begin with soft foods like gelatin, soup and mashed potatoes on the first or the second day post operatively as the child tolerates feeding</p>
<p>The nurse observes the throat directly for evidence of bleeding using a good source of light and if necessary, carefully inserting a tongue depressor.</p>
<p>Other signs of bleeding include tachycardia and pallor, swallowing and vomiting bright red blood, decreasing blood pressure is a late sign.</p>
<p>Check for a cream colored membrane which is normal and often visible on the tonsillar bed post operatively. Check for airway obstruction which may occur due to edema or accumulated secretions and is indicated by signs of respiratory distress, such as a stridor, drooling, restlessness, agitation, increasing respiratory rate, and progressive cyanosis. Suction equipment and oxygen should be available post tonsillectomy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advice-on-discharge">Advice on discharge<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advice-on-discharge" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Advice irritating and highly seasoned food</p>
<p>Avoid use of gargles and vigorous tooth brushing</p>
<p>Discourage the child from coughing or clearing the throat or putting objects in the mouth</p>
<p>Use analgesics or ice collar for pain</p>
<p>Limiting activity to decrease the potential for bleeding, hemorrhage may occur up to 10 days after surgery due to tissue sloughing from the healing process</p>
<p>Report any bleeding</p>
<p>Mouth odor and slight ear pain with low grade fever are common a few days after postoperatively</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="otitis-media">Otitis media<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#otitis-media" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def; Otitis media is an inflammation of the mucous membrane lining the middle ear space.</p>
<p>Three types</p>
<ul>
<li>Acute otitis media</li>
<li>Chronic otitis media- has lasted &gt;3 months</li>
<li>Otitis media with effusion</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>AOM is frequently caused by streptococcus pneumonia, Hemophilus influenza and moraxell catarrhalis, viruses, RSV, and influenza</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most vulnerable group is children below 5 years. Otitis media is primarily as a result of a dysfunctioning Eustachian tube. Obstruction of the Eustachian tube causes accumulation of secretions in the middle ear. Enlarged adenoids, nasopharyngeal tumors, collapse of the tube during swallowing and inefficient opening causing negative pressure which produces transudative middle ear infections, impaired ciliary are some of the causes of dysfunction. When the passage is not totally obstructed, contamination of the middle ear can take place by reflux, aspiration.</p>
<p>14</p>
<p>15</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As purulent fluid accumulates in the small space in the middle ear, pain results from the pressure on the surrounding structures.</p>
<p>Infants are irritable and indicate their discomfort by holding or pulling at their ears and rolling their head from side to side, while older children complain of pain.</p>
<p>Fever, at times up to 40 degrees centigrade</p>
<p>Diarrhea, vomiting and URTI may be present</p>
<p>Due increased pressure the tympanic membrane may rupture resulting in immediate relief of pain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Otoscopic examination- Tympanic membrane is red and bulging.</p>
<p>Serous/purulent fluid behind tympanic membrane</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>Acute otitis media- Treat with antibiotics- Amoxicillin, cefaclor, clotrimoxazole (Bactrim)</p>
<p>For 5-10 days. In case of poor compliance give a single dose of im ceftriaxone (Rocephin)</p>
<p>Serous fluid takes weeks/months to clear.</p>
<p>Recurrent otitis media (occurring within 6 months) need prophylaxis antibiotics treatment and treat URTI early.</p>
<p>Tympanoplasty (myringotomy) is a surgical incision in the tympanic membrane to drain fluid, is indicated if an episode of otitis media with effusion last longer than 3-4 months and associated with loss of 20 Decibels. Ear plugs are used to prevent water entry to the ear when swimming.</p>
<p>During breastfeeding avoid horizontal position and 2nd hand smoking to prevent irritation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-laryngotracheobronchitis">Acute laryngotracheobronchitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-laryngotracheobronchitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="croup">Croup<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#croup" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def; Croup is a group of symptoms characterized by hoarseness, a resonant cough described as 'barking' or 'bassy'(croupy), varying degrees of inspiratory stridor and varying degrees of respiratory distress resulting swelling of the region of the larynx.</p>
<p>Acute laryngotracheobronchitis is the commonest type of croup and affects children less than 5 years of age, and it is inflammation of the mucosa lining the larynx, trachea, and bronchi, causing narrowing of the airway.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Virus parainfluenza virus, RSV, influenza virus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Maintain airway</p>
<p>Nebulized epinephrine which causes mucosal vasoconstriction and subsequent decrease of subglottic oedema</p>
<p>Use of corticosteroids due to their ant inflammatory effects</p>
<p>Give oxygen</p>
<p>If not able to take oral fluids, iv fluid therapy may be indicated</p>
