<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pneumonia">Pneumonia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pneumonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def; Pneumonia is the inflammation of the lung parenchyma. It is common in childhood and affects infants and early childhood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pneumonia can be classified according to morphology, etiological agent or clinical form</p>
<p>16</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="morphological-classification">Morphological classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#morphological-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Lober pneumonia-all or a large segment of one or more pulmonary lobes is involved</p>
<p>Broncho pneumonia-begins in the terminal bronchioles, which become clogged with mucopurulent exudates</p>
<p>Interstitial pneumonia- inflammation process confined within the alveolar walls.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-by-etiological-agent">Classification by etiological agent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-by-etiological-agent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Viral</li>
<li>Bacterial</li>
<li>Mycoplasmal</li>
<li>Aspiration of foreign substances</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-paediatric-guidelines-2016">Kenya paediatric guidelines-2016<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-paediatric-guidelines-2016" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>History of cough or difficulty breathing, age &gt; 60 days</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-severe-pneumonia">1. SEVERE PNEUMONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-severe-pneumonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clinical manifestations</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="one-of-the-danger-signs">One of the danger signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#one-of-the-danger-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxygen saturation &lt;90%</li>
<li>Cyanosis</li>
<li>Inability to drink/breastfeed</li>
<li>AVPU='V', 'P' or 'U' or</li>
<li>Grunting</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit</li>
<li>Oxygen</li>
<li>Penicillin Benzyl Penicillin (Crystalline Penicillin) Age 7 days and over: 50,000 iu/kg/dose 6 hourly IV/IM and</li>
<li>Gentamicin 7.5 mg/kg/24 hr IM or slow IV</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-pneumonia">2. PNEUMONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-pneumonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Lower chest wall indrawing or</li>
<li>Fast breathing (RR 50/min (Age 2-11mo)</li>
<li>RR 40/min (Age 12-59mo)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral Amoxicillin</li>
<li>Counsel carefully on danger signs and need to return if these develop</li>
</ul>
<p>All children must be reviewed within 48 hrs (if review is not Possible admit children with indrawing and treat with amoxicillin)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-no-pneumonia-probably-urti">3. No pneumonia, probably URTI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-no-pneumonia-probably-urti" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>17</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="asthma">Asthma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#asthma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def; Asthma is a chronic inflammatory disorder of the airways in which many cells play a key role. Asthma is characterized by chronic inflammation, bronchoconstriction and bronchial hyper responsiveness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Idiopathic</li>
<li>Allergy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology-of-allergic-types">Pathophysiology of allergic types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-allergic-types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection or allergen causes narrowing of the airways by;</li>
<li>Contraction of the smooth muscles surrounding the airways in the lungs (bronchospasm)</li>
<li>Swelling of the mucosal lining of the airways</li>
<li>Increased secretions in the lumen of the airways</li>
</ul>
<p>Genetic predisposition is an important predisposing factor for asthma. Apart from allergens wheezing can be precipitated in response to exercise and certain drugs.</p>
<p>The classical triad of asthma is cough, dyspnea (breathlessness) and wheezing</p>
<p>Not all children experience these symptoms.</p>
<p>Older children may complain of intermittent chest pain chest tightness.</p>
<p>Episodes of the asthmatic attacks are common at night, with change of season or after exercise.</p>
<p>History of recurrent similar episodes in the past in a child presenting with cough and difficulty in breathing, will be present.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-as-per-kenya-peadiatric-guidelines-2016">Classification as per Kenya peadiatric guidelines 2016<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-as-per-kenya-peadiatric-guidelines-2016" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wheeze + History of cough or difficulty breathing,</p>
<p>(Likelihood of asthma much higher if age &gt; 12m and recurrent wheeze)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="severe-asthma">Severe Asthma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#severe-asthma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any one of these;</p>
<ul>
<li>Oxygen saturation &lt;90%</li>
<li>Central cyanosis</li>
<li>Inability to drink / breast feed</li>
<li>AVPU = "V", "P" or "U" or</li>
<li>Inability to talk/complete sentences</li>
<li>Pulse rate &gt;200 bpm (0-3 yrs) and &gt;180 bpm (4-5yrs)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immediate-management">Immediate Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="admit">ADMIT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#admit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxygen</li>
<li>Nebulize 2.5 mg salbutamol or 6 puff of inhaler with spacer and mask give every 20 minutes upto 3 doses if needed</li>
<li>Prednisolone 2mg/kg</li>
<li>Consider ipratropium bromide 250 mcg if poor response</li>
<li>Antibiotics as for severe pneumonia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mild-or-moderate-asthma">Mild or Moderate Asthma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mild-or-moderate-asthma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wheeze PLUS Lower chest wall indrawing</p>
<p>OR</p>
<ul>
<li>(RR 50/min (Age 2-11mo)</li>
</ul>
<p>RR 40/min (Age 12-59mo)
Fast breathing</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Salbutamol 2 puffs of inhaler (or  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>2.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2.5\mathrm{mg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8389em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">2.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span></span></span></span></span>  nebulized) every 20 minutes upto 3 doses if needed</li>
<li>If mild symptoms allow home on salbutamol MDI give 2 puffs every 6 hours.</li>
<li>Counsel caregiver on signs of deterioration and schedule review within 48 hours.
Monitor closely for 1-2 hours</li>
</ul>
<p>If lack of response to salbutamol, increasing respiratory rate, worsening saturation, any signs of severe asthma. Refer to Immediate Management above</p>
<p>NB Recurrence of asthma symptoms consider inhaled corticosteroid (ICS) therapy or adjusts the doses if already on ICS. (Look out for other comorbidities)</p>
<p>Demonstrate MDI and spacer use to the caregiver before discharge from the health facility. Preferably use spacer with face masks for  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex-error" title="ParseError: KaTeX parse error: Expected 'EOF', got '&amp;' at position 1: &amp;̲lt; 3" style="color: rgb(204, 0, 0);">&amp;lt; 3</span></span>  years for 4-5 years use facemask or mouthpiece</p>
<p>Advise on regular follow up.</p>
<p>Prednisolone administered for 3-5 days. Max dose of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>20</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">y</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">20\mathrm{mg/day}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">20</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg/day</span></span></span></span></span></span>  for  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex-error" title="ParseError: KaTeX parse error: Expected 'EOF', got '&amp;' at position 1: &amp;̲lt; 2" style="color: rgb(204, 0, 0);">&amp;lt; 2</span></span>  years and  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">y</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30\mathrm{mg/day}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">30</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg/day</span></span></span></span></span></span>  for 2-5 years. Repeat Consider ipratropium bromide  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>250</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">250\mathrm{mcg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8389em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">250</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mcg</span></span></span></span></span></span>  every 20 minutes for one hour if needed</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-013e9354.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Use of spacer device and face mask to give bronchodilator treatment. A spacer can be made locally from a plastic soft-drink bottle.</p>
<p>Cardiovascular conditions</p>
<p>Rheumatic fever</p>
<p>Rheumatic fever is a poorly understood inflammatory disease that occurs after pharyngitis caused by Group A beta hemolytic streptococci.</p>
<p>Etiology</p>
<p>This is an immunological disorder caused by damage to the heart by antibodies, which are produced in response to a primary infection of the throat or skin by Group A Beta hemolytic streptococci.</p>
<p>Pathophysiology</p>
<p>The exact pathogenesis is not known. Following untreated streptococcal sore throat there is a latent period that may last from 10 days to several weeks, and during this period there are antibodies from the streptococcal antigen. These antibodies have the capacity to react with human connective tissue, specifically the cardiac muscle. This antigen antibody reaction results in Rheumatic fever.</p>
<p>Mostly affects children aged 5-15 years of age.</p>
<p>Clinical manifestations</p>
<ol>
<li>The first major cardiac manifestation of rheumatic fever is carditis involving endocardium, myocardium, and pericardium</li>
</ol>
<p>Pericarditis present with chest pains and a pericardial rub on auscultation</p>
<p>Myocarditis present with tachycardia, edema, tacypnea and cardiomegally</p>
<p>Endocardial involvement is indicated is indicated by a presence of a thrill and precordial murmurs. Aortic and mitral valves are commonly affected.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>The second major is polyarthritis caused by edema, inflammation and effusions in joint tissue. These nodules are reversible and migratory and favour large joints, such as the knees, elbow, hips, shoulders and wrists. Affected joints are swollen, hot, red and painful for 1-2 days after which another joint is affected. Fever is present in 1-2 weeks and can persist up to 4 weeks in untreated patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The third major manifestation is erythema marginatum –a rash that is reddish, macular and non itching, and predominantly observed on trunk</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The fourth major manifestation is the development of subcutaneous nodules, which are small, non tender swellings that persist after the onset of the disease and gradually resolve with no resulting damage, and may be found on bony prominences such as the feet, hands, elbows, scalp, scapulae and vertebrae.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The last major manifestation which reflects central nervous involvement is chorea also referred to as St.Vitus dance and is characterized by sudden aimless, irregular movement of the extremities, involuntary facial grimaces, speech disturbances, emotional liability and muscle weakness. It is usually exaggerated by anxiety and attempts to use fine motor activity and is relieved by rest.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Diagnosis</p>
<p>Throat culture may be positive or not even though the child has the infection</p>
<p>Echocardiogram for valvular disease</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>In acute phase, the aim to eradicate the organism and decease inflammation process, use oral penicillin as the initial treatment for 10 days or single IM penicillin.</p>
<p>Aspirin- Anti-inflammation- high dose 100/kg/day, then decrease to 70mgs/kg/day, after the acute phase discontinue Aspirin</p>
<p>19</p>
<p>Give antacids because of Aspirin gastric effects
Bed rest until inflammation resolves
Restrict activities because of aortic insufficient/mitral regurgitation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-prophylaxis">Secondary prophylaxis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-prophylaxis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Oral penicillin 250mgs bid or a monthly im injection of penicillin, this is done for at least 10 years or more
Throat infection should be treated timely and does take, avoid under treatment</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rheumatic-heart-disease">Rheumatic heart disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rheumatic-heart-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>RHD is a chronic heart condition caused by RF that can be prevented and controlled. Acute rheumatic fever causes fibrosis of heart valves, leading to crippling valvular heart disease, heart failure and death.
Surgery is often required to repair heart valves in patients with severely damaged valves, the cost of which is high and a drain on the limited health resources of poor countries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anaemia">Anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anaemia is a condition marked by a deficiency of red blood cells or of hemoglobin in the blood, resulting in pallor and weakness. Anaemia is not a disease but a manifestation of underlying pathologic process</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Etiology has manifested by erythrocyte or hemoglobin depletion</li>
<li>Morphology, the characteristic changes in RBC size, shape and color</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Inadequate production of RBC or RBC components</li>
<li>Increased destruction of RBC</li>
<li>Excessive loss of RBC through hemorrhage</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The basic physiologic defect caused by anemia is a decrease in oxygen carrying capacity of blood which leads to a reduction in the amount of oxygen available to the cells. When the anaemia develops slowly, the child usually adapts to the declining hemoglobin level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="red-blood-cell-morphology">Red blood cell morphology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#red-blood-cell-morphology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="size">Size<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#size" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Normocytes-normal RBC
Microcytes- Smaller than normal RBC
Macrocytes- Larger than normal RBC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="shape">Shape<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shape" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Spherocytes-Globular cells
Drepanocytes-Sickle shaped cells
Numerous-Other irregularly shaped cells</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="color">Color<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#color" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Normochromic-Normal amount of hemoglobin per red blood cell
Hypochromic-Reduced amount of hemoglobin per red blood cell
Hyperchromic-Increased amount of hemoglobin per red blood cell</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-anemia">Signs and symptoms of anemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-anemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pallor
Tachycardia
Fatigue, headache</p>
<p>20</p>
<p>Muscle weakness
Systolic heart murmur due to decreased red call production
Frontal bossing
Jaundice
Dark urine
Splenomegaly
Hepatomegaly
Low blood pressure- a late sign of shock
Decreased peripheral pulses due to increased red cell loss</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical presentation and history</li>
<li>Capillary blood count and hematocrit levels will show low numbers of red blood cell, low hemoglobin, low hematocrit, low reticulocytes (which indicate the body’s response to an increased demand for red blood cells). A peripheral smear may demonstrate significant changes in the shape of red blood cells such as sickled cells</li>
<li>Bone marrow aspirates-which will show the body’s ability to produce normal cells</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Objective is to reverse the anaemia by treating the underlying cause
In nutritional anaemia’s the specific deficiency is treated
In blood loss from acute hemorrhage, red blood cell transfusion may be given
In patients with severe anaemia, supportive medical care may include oxygen therapy, bed rest and replacement of intravenous volume with intravenous fluids
A detailed history is necessary on nutrition, history of chronic illness, recurrent infections, eating habits, particularly pica (consumption of non nutritive substances such as soil), bowel habits, and presence of blood in stools, familial history of hereditary diseases such as sickle cell disease and Thalassemia.
Assess the child’s level of tolerance for activities of daily living and play and make adjustments to allow as much self care as possible without undue exertion
Do vital signs and have a baseline when at rest and monitor the difference after activities</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevent-complications">Prevent complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevent-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Children with anaemia are prone to infection and their immune system is weak
Protect infections by hand washing, selecting a room in a non infectious area, restricting the presence of visitors or hospital personnel with active infection and maintain adequate nutrition
Observe for signs of heart failure. So prevent this by administering oxygen to minimize hypoxia and closely monitor intravenous fluids and administer packed red blood cells.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diarrhea">Diarrhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diarrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diarrhea is the frequent discharge of semi-solid or liquid faecal matter from the bowels. Diarrhea is a symptom that results from disorders involving digestive, absorptive and secretory functions. It is caused by abnormal intestinal water and electrolyte transport
Types of diarrhea</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute">Acute<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acute diarrhea is a leading cause of illness in children younger than five years of age which is defined as a sudden increase in frequency and a change in consistency of stools, often caused by infections agents in the GIT tract. Acute diarrhea is usually self limiting &lt;14 days duration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>21</p>
<p>Most pathogens which spread diarrhea are spread by the fecal-oral route through contaminated food or water or from person to person where there is close contact e.g. day care centers, lack of clean water, crowding poor hygiene, nutritional deficiency and poor sanitation are major risk factors. Infants are more susceptible to frequent and severe bouts of diarrhea due to poor immune system</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-acute-diarrhea">Causes of acute diarrhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-acute-diarrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bacteria e.g. salmonella, shigella, campylobacter, Escherichia coli, clostrium dificile, staphylococcus aureus</li>
<li>Viruses-Rota virus which causes about 70% of diarrhea, adenovirus</li>
<li>Parasites- Girdia lamblia, entamoeba histolytica</li>
<li>Associated conditions e.g URTI, UTI, otitis media</li>
<li>Dietary causes e.g over feeding, introducing new foods, osmotic diarrhea from excess sugar in formula or juice</li>
<li>Medications- Antibiotics, laxatives</li>
<li>Toxic substances- Ingestion of heavy metals (arsenic, lead, mercury) organic phosphates</li>
<li>Functional causes – Irritable bowels syndrome</li>
<li>Other causes- Hirshsprung enterocolitis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-diarrhea">Chronic diarrhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-diarrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chronic diarrhea is an increase in stool frequency and increased water content within duration of more than 14 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Malabsorption syndromes</li>
<li>Inflammatory bowel disease</li>
<li>Immunodeficiency</li>
<li>Food allergy</li>
<li>Lactulose intolerance</li>
<li>Or chronic non specific diarrhea as a result of inadequate management of acute diarrhea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Invasion of the GIT tract by pathogens results in increased intestinal secretion as a result of enterotoxins, cytotoxic mediators (those damaging the cell) and decreased intestinal absorption secondary to intestinal damage or inflammation. The most serious and immediate physiologic disturbances associated with severe diarrhea diarrheal disease are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>Acid base balance with acidosis</li>
<li>Shock that occurs when dehydration progresses to the point that circulatory status is seriously impaired</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>History- Ask about recent travel, exposure to untreated drinking water or washing water sources etc</p>
<p>Stool for ova/cyst</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-diarrhoea-gastroenteritis">Management of Diarrhoea / Gastroenteritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-diarrhoea-gastroenteritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>History of diarrhoea / vomiting, age &gt; 1 months</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypovolaemic-shock-from-diarrhoea-dehydration">Hypovolaemic shock from diarrhoea / dehydration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypovolaemic-shock-from-diarrhoea-dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="all-four-of">All four of<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#all-four-of" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Weak/absent pulse;</li>
<li>AVPU &lt; A;</li>
<li>Cold hands + Temp gradient;</li>
</ul>
<p>22</p>
<ul>
<li>Capillary refill &gt; 3 secs
PLUS sunken eyes and
slow skin pinch
NB: If Hb &lt; 5 g/dl, transfuse urgently</li>
</ul>
<p>Ringer’s 20 mls/kg a second bolus may be given if required before proceeding to step 2 of Plan C (see below)
Treat for Hypoglycaemia</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="severe-dehydration">SEVERE DEHYDRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#severe-dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="plan-c">(Plan c)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plan-c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unable to drink or AVUP &lt; A plus;
Sunken eyes
Return of skin pinch ≥ 2 secs</p>
<p>Step 1- 30 mls/kg Ringer’s over 30 mins if ≥ 12m OR
Over 60 mins if age &lt; 12m
Step 2- 70 mls/kg Ringer’s over 2.5 hrs if age ≥ 12m OR
Over 5 hrs if age &lt; 12m
Start ORS at 5 mls/kg/hr, once able to drink
OR
NG rehydration-120mls/kg ors over 6 hrs
NB Re-assess at least hourly and after 3-6hrs, re-classty as sever some or ni dehydration and treat accordingly</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="some-dehydration">SOME Dehydration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#some-dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Able to drink adequately but 2 or more of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sunken eyes</li>
<li>Return of skin pinch 1 - 2 secs</li>
<li>Restlessness / irritability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="plan-b">Plan B<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plan-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>ORS by mouth at 75 mls/kg over 4 hrs, plus,</li>
<li>Continue breast feeding as tolerated</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Sunken eyes
Reassess at 4 hrs &amp; treat according to classification</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="no-dehydration">NO Dehydration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#no-dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diarrhoea with fewer than 2 of the above signs of dehydration</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="plan-a">Plan A<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plan-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>10mls/kg ORS after each loose stool</li>
<li>Continue breast feeding and encourage feeding if &gt; 6 months</li>
</ol>
<p>All cases to receive Zinc. Antimicrobials are NOT indicated unless there is dysentery or proven amoebiasis or giardiasis.</p>
<p>23</p>
<p>Urinary tract infections</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="urinary-tract-infection">Urinary tract infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urinary-tract-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Urinary tract infection (UTI) is a clinical condition that may involve the urethra and bladder (lower urinary tract) and ureters, renal pelvis, calyces and renal parenchyma (upper urinary tract). Since it is impossible to localize the infection, the term UTI is applied to the presence of significant numbers of micro-organisms anywhere within the urinary tract (except the lower third of the urethra which is usually colonized by bacteria).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="classification-of-uti-or-inflammations">Classification of UTI or inflammations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-uti-or-inflammations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Bacteriuria- Presence of bacteria in urine</p>
<p>Asymptomatic bacteriuria- Bacteria accompanied by physical signs of urinary infection, dysuria, suprapubic discomfort, hematuria, fever)</p>
<p>Recurrent urinary tract infection-Repeated episode of bacteriuria or symptomatic UTI</p>
<p>Persistent UTI- Persistence of bacteriuria despite antibiotic treatment</p>
<p>Febrile UTI- Bacteria accompanied by fever and other physical signs</p>
<p>Cystitis- Inflammation of the bladder</p>
<p>Urethritis- Inflammation of the urethra</p>
<p>Pyelonephritis- Inflammation of the upper urinary tract and kidneys</p>
<p>Urosepsis- Febrile UTI coexisting with systemic signs of bacterial illness, blood culture reveals presence of urinary pathogens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A number of organisms are responsible for UTI, Escherichia (coli 80%), and other gram negative enteric organisms associated with UTI. Other organisms associated with UTI include proteus, pseudomonas, klebsiella, staphylococcus aureus, haemophilus.</p>
<p>A number of factors contribute to the development of UTI including anatomical, physical and conditions or properties of the host's urinary tract.</p>
<p>In females- the short urethra and the closure of the urethra at the end of micturation may return contaminated urine by bacteria to the bladder</p>
<p>The longer male urethra(in an adult) and the antibacterial properties of prostatic secretions inhibit the entry and growth of micro-organisms, the presence or absence of the foreskin contributes to the differences in UTI rates in infants</p>
<p>Urine that remains in the bladder allows bacteria from the urethra to rapidly become established in the rich medium</p>
<p>Incomplete emptying of the bladder can cause UTI, which could result from anatomic abnormalities, (esp. those of the ureters) or bladder compression.</p>
<p>The pressure of over distension within the bladder may increase the risk of infection by decreasing the host resistance probably due to decreased blood flow.</p>
<p>Other factors include constipation which displaces the bladder and posterior urethra in a fixed and limited space of the bony pelvis, causing obstruction, incomplete micturation and urinary stasis, failure to relieve the impaction in spite of adequate treatment of UTI mat result to recurrence</p>
<p>Other causes of UTI include urinary catheters, tight clothing, diapers, poor hygiene, local inflammation, vaginitis, masturbation or pin worm infestation may increase the risk of ascending infection. Essential oils in bubble baths and shampoos can irritate the urethra causing painful and frequent urination. Sexual intercourse is associated with increased risk of UTI.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>After bacteria invasion by bacteria, the host first line of defense in the lower urinary tract is complete evacuation by voiding. Inflammation in the bladder and urethral walls is apparent within 30 minutes of invasion by a bacterial pathogen. Polymorphonuclear leukocytes rapidly migrate to the bladder which becomes infected within 2 hours, complete evacuation of the bladder is particularly important for the eradication of bacteria from</p>
<p>the urine. Urination removes bacteria and associated toxins contained in urine and allow more efficient destruction of the bacteria remaining on the thin film of urine that is closely adheres to the vesical wall</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="depend-with-age">Depend with age<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#depend-with-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Infants and children &lt; 2 years of age the signs are non specific and they more resemble GIT disorders, which include failure to thrive, feeding problems, vomiting, diarrhea, abdominal distension, and jaundice. Newborns may have fever, hypothermia or sepsis, frequent or infrequent voiding, constant irritability, strong smelling urine and an abnormal stream. A persistent diaper rash is also a helpful clue. Children &gt; 2 years of age the classic symptoms include enuresis or daytime incontinence in a child who has been toilet trained, fever strong or foul smelling urine, increased frequency of urination, dysuria or urgency or urgency. They may also complain of abdominal pain or flank pain. Some present with hematuria, some may present (boys) dribbling of urine, straining with urination or a decrease in the force and size of the stream, high fever and chills, leukocytosis suggest pyelonephritis. Adolescent have more specific symptoms—include frequency and painful urination of a turbulent urine that may be bloody, fever is usually absent, however upper tract infection is characterized by fever, chills, frank pain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This depends on a high degree of suspicion, history taking and physical examination</p>
<p>Urine sample with possible infection appears cloudy, hazy or thick with noticeable strands of mucus and pus; it also smells fishy and unpleasant</p>
<p>Presumptive diagnosis; Urine test may reveal, pyuria and presence of bacteria, also normal urine may present in conditions of asymptomatic bacteriuria</p>
<p>Detection of bacteria in a urine culture confirms the diagnosis of UTI, but urine collection is often difficult esp. in infants and small children, which may lead to contamination of a specimen by organisms from other sources. Bag urine specimens are commonly contaminated.</p>
<p>Unless the specimen is a first morning sample, a recent high fluid intake may indicate a fasely low organism count. Therefore do not encourage children to drink large volumes of water in an attempt to obtain a specimen quickly. The most accurate tests of bacterial content are suprapubic aspiration and properly performed bladder catheterization (as long as the first few mls are excluded from collection). The urine specimen for culture should be taken to the laboratory immediately, if culture is delayed place the sample in a refrigerator for up to 24 hours, but storage can result in a loss of formed elements. Presence of nitrites on dipstick analysis identifies infected urine and absence of nitrites and leukocyte in combination identifies infected urine. These test results are used to initiate treatment of UTI while culture results are pending some organisms are non-nitrite producing e.g. pseudomonas organisms.</p>
<p>Localization of the infection may involve more specific tests including ureteral catherization, bladder washout procedures, radio isotope renography, ultrasonography, intravenous pyelography.</p>
<p>NB. For the best results, wash the perineal area thoroughly before applying the urine collection bag, and promptly remove the bag as soon as voiding occurs. Leaving the device in situ for more than one hour is more likely to yield a contaminated urine specimen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives-for-treatment-are">Objectives for treatment are;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-for-treatment-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Eliminate current infection</li>
<li>Identify contributing factors to reduce risk of recurrence</li>
<li>Prevent orosepsis</li>
<li>Preserve renal function</li>
</ul>
<p>Antibiotics therapy are prescribed on the basis of culture results, however empiric therapy on the basis of child's history and presenting symptoms may be necessary. Antibiotics in use include penicillins,</p>
<p>25</p>
<p>sulphonamides (including trimethoprin sulfamethoxale), the cephalosporins, nitrofurantoin and the tetracyclines. Children with suspected pyelonephritis and fever are admitted to the hospital and given appropriate antibiotics intravenously for a minimum of 48 hours. Blood and urine cultures are done on admission and after therapy, and therefore repeated at monthly intervals for 3 months and 3 months interval for another six months. Renal scarring can develop during the initial infection esp. in younger children and therefore the first UTI in childhood necessitates radiological examination</p>
<p>Anatomical defects such as bladder neck obstruction or bladder reflux may require surgical correction to prevent recurrent infection or may indicate the need for prophylactic antibiotics and careful follow up monitoring since relapse rate is high and recurrent infection tends to occur 1 to 2 months after termination of treatment. The aim of the therapy and careful follow up in such cases to prevent morbidity and reduce the chance of renal scarring</p>
<p>Educate the parents and children on prevention and treatment of infection</p>
<p>Encourage adequate fluid intake for the prevention and treatment of UTI, since bacterial eradication from the urinary tract is partially dependent on urine flow and voiding frequently, patient to drink clear fluids, children to avoid caffeinated and carbonated beverages because of their potentially irritable effect on bladder mucosa. A child who is febrile and unable to drink liquids is given intravenous hydration until the fever resolves and oral liquid is given intravenous hydration until fever resolves and oral liquids are tolerated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>With prompt and adequate treatment at the time of diagnosis, the long term prognosis for UTI's is usually excellent. When infection occurs in young children &lt; 2 years of age there is a greater hazard of progressive renal injury and is associated with congenital renal malformations and reflux, therefore early diagnosis is important.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-glomerulonephritis">Acute glomerulonephritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-glomerulonephritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is sudden inflammation of glomeruli within the kidney which results in acute renal failure. Glomerulus gets damaged, hence referred as intrarenal acute renal failure. It may affect glomerular capillaries or membrane</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incidence">Incidence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incidence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Glomerulonephritis can occur at any age but has a peak age of onset of 6 to 7 years and rare in children &lt;2 years. Common in boys than girls</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infectious agent is usually in the body 2-3 weeks before clinical manifestation and it could be bacterial (streptococcus group A commonest) e.g. acute post streptococcal glomerulonephritis or viral</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The mechanism by which the reaction takes place is still speculative. The most popular proposal to explain the pathologic process is that the streptococcal infection is followed by a release of a membrane like material from the specific organism into the circulation, and since it is antigenic, antibodies are formed and an immune complex reaction occurs after the appropriate period. These immune complexes become trapped in the glomerular capillary loop and inflammation occurs. End result is scarred/ damaged glomeruli, membrane permeability altered by immune response. Protein leak into urine, glomeruli filtration rate decreases, sodium and water are retained and oedema occurs, cause of elevated BP is not explained</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="heamaturia">Heamaturia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heamaturia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Dependent and periobital oedema and puffiness of the face and oedema is more prominent in the morning</p>
<p>26</p>
<p>Diminished urinary output</p>
<p>Proteinuria</p>
<p>Increased BP</p>
<p>Fatigue</p>
<p>Decreased filtration</p>
<p>Increased serum sodium level and increased potassium levels</p>
<p>Increased BUN and creatinine</p>
<p>Low grade fever</p>
<p>Urine becomes blood tinged, smoky or tea coloured or cola coloured urine</p>
<p>Anorexia</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clinical manifestations</p>
<p>Physical exam</p>
<p>Immunological test to detect streptozyme and serum complement</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Depend on the kidney damage</p>
<p>The aim is to treat source of inflammation and maintain fluid and electrolytes and maintain the BP within normal range</p>
<p>Bed rest is no longer recommended during the acute phase because ambulation does not seem to have an adverse event on the course of the disease. During acute phase children are listless and experience fatigue and malaise, most children restrict their activities.</p>
<p>Fluid balance</p>
<p>Do vital signs, body weight (daily), intake and output (daily)</p>
<p>Water intake is calculated, insensible loss plus the volume of urine passed.</p>
<p>Diuretic therapy is helpful when renal is not severe. In case of severe renal failure diuretic therapy is not useful.</p>
<p>Hypertension: Take BP readings 4 to 6 hours, and in case of elevated BP start on antihypertensive drugs such as calcium channel blockers, beta blockers or angiotensin- converting enzyme inhibitors</p>
<p>Monitor seizures associated with hypertensive encephalopathy and incase of seizures give anticonvulsants.</p>
<p>Nutrition: Limit sodium intake- moderate sodium intake restriction, protein intake restrictions to those with azotemia and prolonged oliguria</p>
<p>Antibiotics are indicated only for children with evidence of persistent streptococcal infections</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nephrotic-syndrome">Nephrotic syndrome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nephrotic-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nephrotic syndrome is defined as massive proteinuria, hypoalbuminemia, hyperlipidemia and edema</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types">Types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Primary nephrotic syndrome is when the syndrome is restricted to glomerular injury</p>
<p>Secondary nephritic syndrome when it develops as part of a systemic illness e.g. toxins, lead poisoning</p>
<p>Congenital nephritic syndrome- infant with nephritic syndrome within 3 months of life are considered congenital e.g. due to autosomal recessive disorder</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cause">Cause<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cause" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Idiopathic, is thought to be caused by immune response while the other is caused by infections, drugs and toxins</p>
<p>Common in males than females 2:1, it commonly affects those aged between 2 to 6 years.</p>
<p>27</p>
<p>28</p>
