<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The inflammation process from immune response or disease makes glomeruli to become permeable to proteins (proteinuria), this reduces serum albumin level (hypoalbuminemia), fluid shift from the intravascular space to interstitial space which subsequently leads to oedema/ ascites which lead to hypovolemia, this in turn stimulates the rennin angiotensin system and the secretion of antidiuretic hormone and aldosterone. Tubular reabsorption of sodium and water increases in an attempt to increase intravascular volume. The elevation of lipids is not fully understood</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Puffness of the face, around the eyes mostly in the morning and subsides later during the day, swelling of the abdomen and lower extremities</p>
<p>Anorexia, irritability, abdominal pain and diarrhea (due to edema of the interstitial mucosa)</p>
<p>Volume of urine is decreased and appears darkly opalescent and frothy</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Dependent on proteinuria</p>
<p>Clinical manifestations</p>
<p>Reduced total serum protein (&lt;2g/dl)</p>
<p>Renal biopsy- can show the type of nephrotic syndrome</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The primary aim is to reduce the excretion of urinary protein and maintain protein free urine; additional objectives include treatment of acute infection, control of oedema, and establishment of good nutrition and readjustment of any disturbed metabolic processes</p>
<p>General principle is generally supportive</p>
<p>Diet- During the period of massive oedema and corticosteroid therapy salt is restricted; a diet rich in protein is logical, however in case of azotemia or renal failure restrict high protein diet.</p>
<p>Corticosteroid therapy- administer per oral 60 mg/m²/day in evenly divided doses- use prednisolone continue od × 6 weeks, then decrease to 40 mg/m² alternate days for more 6 weeks (should be continued for at least 3 months)</p>
<p>Immunosuppressant therapy is used to reduce the relapse rate and induce long-term remission in children with frequent relapsing or steroid resistance nephrotic syndrome, oral cyclophosphamide or chlorambucil, cyclosporine</p>
<p>Diuretics like frusemide can be used, but monitor sodium, potassium, and hypovolemia</p>
<p>Antibiotics may be required in case of infection</p>
<p>Nursing- prevent infection and skin breakdown</p>
<p>Fluid restriction if child is hyponatremic</p>
<p>Elevate swollen scrotum with pillows to enhance the removal of fluid by gravity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="meningococcal-meningitis">Meningococcal meningitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningococcal-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Bacterial meningitis is an acute inflammation of the meninges and CSF</p>
<p>Meningococcal meningitis occurs in epidermic form and is the only type readily transmitted by droplet infection from nasopharyngeal secretions</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The causative organism of meningococcal meningitis is neisseria meningitidis, also called meningococcus. Although this condition may develop at any age, the risk of meningococcal infection increases with the number of contacts, therefore it occurs in school –age children and adolescents and appears to be some seasonal variations. Meningitis caused by pneumococcal infections or meningococcal infections occur at any time</p>
<p>Maternal factors such as premature rupture of fetal membranes and maternal infection during the last weeks of pregnancy are major causes of neonatal meningitis</p>
<p>Risk factors for developing meningitis include recent exposure to someone with meningococcal meningitis, recent ear infections or sinus infection, travel to areas where bacterial meningitis is common, penetrating head trauma, cochlear input devices, and anatomic defects such as dermal sinus, urinary tract anomaly or recent placement of ventricular shunt</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most common route of infection is vascular dissemination from a focus of infection elsewhere.e.g. organisms from nasopharynx invade the underlying blood vessels, cross the blood brain barrier and multiply in the CSF. The infective process is that of inflammation, exudation, white blood cell accumulation and varying degrees of tissue damage. The brain becomes hyperemic and edematous and the entire surface of the brain is covered by a layer of purulent exudates. As the infection extends to the ventricles, thick pus, fibrin or adhesions may occlude the narrow passage s and obstruct the flow of CSF</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Usually abrupt on onset with;</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Chills</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Altered conscious level</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
<li>Irritability</li>
<li>Agitation</li>
<li>Neck rigidity</li>
<li>Kerning’s sign and brudzinski positive in children and adolescent</li>
<li>Petechial or purpuric rash</li>
<li>Poor feeding / breastfeeding</li>
<li>Neonatal bulging of the fontanelle</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lumber puncture is the definitive diagnostic test</li>
<li>CSF- culture and sensitivity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute bacterial meningitis is a medical emergency and requires early recognition and immediate therapy to prevent death and residual disabilities</li>
<li>Isolation precautions</li>
<li>Antibiotics – preferably cephalosporins</li>
<li>Maintenance hydration</li>
<li>Maintenance of ventilation by positioning the patient</li>
<li>Reduction of increased intracranial pressure by elevating the bed</li>
<li>Management of systemic shock</li>
<li>Control of seizures</li>
<li>Control of temperature</li>
</ul>
<p>29</p>
<p>30</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="malnutrition">Malnutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Malnutrition is lack of proper nutrition, caused by not having enough to eat, not eating enough of the right things, or being unable to use the food that one does eat. It is a major health condition affecting under 5 years of age. The most extreme forms of malnutrition or protein-energy malnutrition are kwashiorkor and marasmus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Diarrhea (gastroenteritis) is a major factor</p>
<p>Other factors are bottle feeding (in poor sanitary conditions)</p>
<p>Inadequate knowledge of proper child care practices</p>
<p>Parental illiteracy</p>
<p>Economic and political factors</p>
<p>Climate conditions</p>
<p>Cultural and religious food preferences</p>
<p>Lack of adequate food</p>
<p>PEM may also be seen in persons with chronic health problems</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In general, marasmus is an insufficient energy intake to match the body's requirements. As a result the body draws on its own stores, resulting in emaciation.</p>
<p>In kwashiorkor, adequate carbohydrate consumption and decreased protein intake lead to decreased synthesis of visceral proteins. The resulting hypoalbuminemia contributes to extravascular fluid accumulation; impaired synthesis of B- lipoprotein produces fatty liver. PEM also involves, an inadequate intake of many essential nutrients, low serum levels of zinc have been implicated as the cause of skin ulceration in many patients</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kwashiorkor">Kwashiorkor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kwashiorkor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Kwashiorkor is defined as primarily a deficiency of protein with an adequate supply of calories in form of carbohydrates but inadequate amount of proteins. The term is taken from the Ga language of Ghana and means 'the sickness of the weaning'</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The child with kwashiorkor has thin, wasted extremities and a prominent abdomen from oedema (ascitis) and the oedema often masks severe muscular atrophy</p>
<p>The skin is scaly and dry and has areas of depigmentation</p>
<p>Dermatoses of the skin may be evident, partly resulting from vitamin deficiencies.</p>
<p>Permanent blindness often results from lack of vitamin A</p>
<p>Acute zinc deficiency is a common complication of severe PEM and results in skin rashes, loss of hair, impaired immune response and susceptibility to infections, digestive problems, night blindness, and changes in mood, defective wound healing and impaired growth. Its depressant effects limits food intake. The hair is thin, dry, coarse and dull. Depigmentation is common and patchy alopecia may occur.</p>
<p>Diarrhea occurs from lowered resistance to infection and further complicates electrolyte imbalance</p>
<p>Anaemia is also a common finding in malnourished children.</p>
<p>Protein deficiency increases the child's susceptibility to infection which can result to death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marasmus">Marasmus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marasmus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Marasmus results from general malnutrition of both calories and protein. Marasmus is usually a syndrome of physical and emotional deprivation. Marasmus is derived from the Greek word marasmus, which means withering or wasting. Marasmus involves inadequate intake of protein and calories and is characterized by emaciation.</p>
<p>Marasmic kwashiorkor is a form of PEM in which clinical findings of both kwashiorkor and marasmus are evident.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Marasmus is characterized by gradual wasting and atrophy of body tissues, especially of subcutaneous fat. The child appears to be very old, with loose and wrinkled skin. Fat metabolism is less impaired than in kwashiorkor, thus deficiency of fat soluble vitamins is usually minimal or absent. The child is fretful (constantly worried), apathetic, withdrawn and so lethargic that prostration frequently occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="measuring-nutritional-status">Measuring nutritional status<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measuring-nutritional-status" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Anthropometry (body measurement) quantifies malnutrition. In children, measurement of mid-upper arm circumference (MUAC) is the most simple.</p>
<p>Weight and height measurements can be useful to detect wasting and stunting and individual monitoring over time e.g. growth velocity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="mid-upper-arm-circumference-muac">Mid upper arm circumference (MUAC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mid-upper-arm-circumference-muac" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>MUAC is measured using a tape around the left upper arm. MUAC is quicker in sick patients so use MUAC in acute management.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-c0cd25cd.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="weight-height-and-age">Weight, Height and Age<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weight-height-and-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Weight for height (W/H): Measure length lying if aged &lt;2 y to give weight for length. Low W/H (or W/L) = wasting, and indicates acute malnutrition.</p>
<p>Weight for age (W/A): Low W/A does not distinguish acute from chronic malnutrition. W/A is thus not used for diagnosis of acute malnutrition, but can be used to monitor growth e.g. in the MCH booklet</p>
<p>In the diagnosis of acute malnutrition we use W/H expressed as Z scores. Z - scores can be obtained from simple tables</p>
<p>Visible Severe Wasting tends to identify only severest cases of SAM. It is better to use MUAC or WHZ score.</p>
<p>Kwashiorkor = severe malnutrition (at any age)</p>
<p>32</p>
<p>Classifying malnutrition
(for WHZ values)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Acute Malnutrition (severity)</th><th>MUAC (cm)</th><th>WHZ</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>None</td><td>&gt;13.5</td><td>&gt; - 1</td></tr><tr><td>At Risk</td><td>12.5 to 13.4</td><td>&gt; - 2 to &lt; 1</td></tr><tr><td>Moderate</td><td>11.5 to 12.4</td><td>&gt; - 3 to &lt; - 2</td></tr><tr><td>Severe</td><td>&lt; 11.5</td><td>&lt; - 3</td></tr><tr><td>Severe</td><td>Kwashiorkor</td><td>Kwashiorkor</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="complicated-severe-acute-malnutrition">Complicated severe acute malnutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complicated-severe-acute-malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>age 6 - 59 months</p>
<p>Check using ABC approach and admit if acute illness and either of:</p>
<ul>
<li>MUAC &lt; 11.5 cm (or visible severe wasting if no MUAC) with WHZ &lt; 3 used if child aged &lt; 6 months</li>
<li>Oedema / other signs of Kwashiokor (flaky pale skin /h air changes)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-1">Step 1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Check blood glucose and treat if &lt; 3 mmol/l (5 m ls/kg 1 0% dextrose
If glucose test unavailable treat for hypoglycaemia if not alert</li>
<li>Oral / NG glucose or feeds should as soon as possible (not &gt; 30 mins after admission)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-2">Step 2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Check for hypothermia, axillary temperature &lt;35°C.</li>
<li>If present warm with blankets, warm bags of fluid or a heater</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-3">Step 3<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Check for dehydration if has diarrhoea. If in shock, use IV fluids if not in shock use ReSoMal</p>
<ul>
<li>Transfuse if Hb &lt; 4 g/dL, 10mls/kg whole blood in 3hrs + frusemide 1mg/kg</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-4">Step 4<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-4" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Electrolyte imbalance. Use commercial F75. If not available mineral mix and 4 mmol/kg/day of oral potassium may need to be added to feeds, Never use Frusemide for oedema!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-5">Step 5<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-5" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>All ill children with SAM should get IV Penicillin (or Ampicillin) AND Gentamicin. Give 5 days gentamicin, if improved change Pen to Amoxicillin at 48 hrs. Add:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nystatin / Clotrimazole for oral thrush if present</li>
<li>Albendazole after 7 days treatment.</li>
<li>TEO (+ atropine drops) for pus / ulceration in the eye</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-6">Step 6<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-6" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Correct micronutrient deficiencies. Give:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Vitamin A (PO) if eye signs on admission and days 2 and 14.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Multivits for at least 2 weeks if no RUTF or F75/F100</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Folic acid 2.5mg alt days if no RUTF or F75/F100</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iron ONLY when child is gaining weight &amp; If no RUTF</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-7">Step 7<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Prescribe feeding needed (see chart) and place ng.</p>
<p>Steps 8, 9 &amp; 10: Ensure appetite and weight are monitored and start catch-up feeding with RUTF or F100 (usually day 3-7). Provide a caring and stimulating environment for the child and start educating the family so they help in the acute treatment and are ready for discharge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fluid-management-in-severe-malnutrition-with-diarrhoea">Fluid management in severe malnutrition with diarrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluid-management-in-severe-malnutrition-with-diarrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="shock">Shock:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>AVPU&lt;A, plus absent, or weak pulse plus prolonged capillary refilling (&gt;3s) plus cold periphery with temperature gradient 20 mls/kg in 2 hrs of Ringer’s lactate with 5% dextrose – add 50 mls 50% dextrose to 450 mls Ringer’s lactate</p>
<p>If severe anaemia start urgent blood transfusion not Ringer’s.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="if-not-in-shock-or-after-treating-shock">If not in shock or after treating shock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-not-in-shock-or-after-treating-shock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>If unable to give oral / ngt fluid because of very poor medical condition use / continue with iv fluids at maintenance regimen of 4mls/kg/hr</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="if-able-to-introduce-oral-or-ng-fluids-feeds">If able to introduce oral or ng fluids / feeds:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-able-to-introduce-oral-or-ng-fluids-feeds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>For 2 hours: Give ReSoMal at 10mls/kg/hour</p>
<p>Then: Give ReSoMal at 7.5ml/kg over 1 hour then introduce first feed with F75 and alternate ReSoMal with F75 each hour at 7.5mls/kg/hr for 10 hours - can increase or decrease hourly fluid as tolerated between 5 - 10 mls/kg/hr.</p>
<p>At 12 hours switch to 3 hourly oral / NG feeds with F75</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="feeding-children-with-severe-malnutrition-age-6-59-months">Feeding children with severe malnutrition (age 6 - 59 months)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#feeding-children-with-severe-malnutrition-age-6-59-months" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>If aged &lt; 6 months use EBM or term formula or use diluted F100 - to each 100mls F100 add 35mls clean water</li>
<li>When appetite returns (and oedema much improved) change from F75 to F100 at 130mls/kg (the same volume as F75 for no oedema) in the transition phase (about 2 days), if F100 not available change to RUTF for transition phase.</li>
<li>After transition phase use RUTF that has 500 kcal in 92g packets for rehabilitation. All vitamins, minerals and iron are in RUTF. Allow the child to nibble RUTF very frequently. RUTF can be mixed into uji or other foods slowly introduced.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2ec12a72">F75 – acute feeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2ec12a72" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>No or moderate oedema (130mls/kg/day)</p>
<p>Severe oedema, even face (100mls/kg/day)</p>
<p>If respiratory distress or oedema gets worse or the jugular veins are engorged reduce feed volumes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="f100-transition-phase">F100 Transition phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f100-transition-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Replace starter F-75 with an equal amount of catch-up F-100 for 2 days.</p>
<p>On the third day if on F-100, increase each successive feed by 10 ml until some feed remains uneaten (usually at 200ml/kg/day).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="f100-rehabilitation-phase">F100 Rehabilitation phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f100-rehabilitation-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Monitor vital signs. If both pulse and breathing rates increase (breathing by 5 breaths/min and pulse by 25 beats/min), sustained for two successive 4-hourly readings, then:
Reduce the volume fed to 100 ml/kg per day for 24 h.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="malignancies">Malignancies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malignancies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="16bec3f4">Wilm’s tumour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#16bec3f4" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Wilm’s tumour or nephroblastoma is a malignant tumour of the kidney and is the most common kidney tumour of childhood and common below 5 years of age. About 2% of Wilm’s tumour is family related</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Painless swelling or mass within the abdomen. The mass is firm, non tender, confined to one side, and deep within the flank.</li>
<li>Other signs and symptoms are the result of compression from the tumor mass, metabolic alterations secondary to tumor or metastasis</li>
<li>Haematuria</li>
<li>Anaemia due to hemorrhage within the tumor- occur occasionary</li>
<li>Weight loss and fever</li>
<li>Metastasis to the lungs- dyspnea, cough, shortness of breath and pain may be present</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>History and physical examination</strong>
Signs of malignancy such as weight loss, enlarged liver and spleen, anemia and enlarged lymph nodes
Radiological studies, e.g. abdominal ultrasound, CT (computed tomography) and MRI (magnetic resonance imaging) of the abdomen
Complete blood count- increased RBC present if tumor is secreting excess erythropoietin</p>
<p><strong>Staging of Wilm’s tumor</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Stage 1. Tumor is limited to kidney and completely resected</li>
<li>Stage 2. Tumor extends beyond kidney but is completely resected</li>
<li>Stage 3. Residual non hematogenous tumor to abdomen</li>
<li>Stage 4. Hematogenous metastasis, deposits are beyond stage 3 namely to lung, liver, bone and brain</li>
<li>Stage 5. Billateral tumor involvement is present at diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Surgery and chemotherapy with or without radiation, is based on the clinical stage and histological pattern. The most effective agents for treating Wilm’s tumour are actinomycin D and vincristine, doxorubicin and cyclophosphamide</p>
<p>Nursing care include preparation for diagnostic and operative procedures</p>
<p>Explanation of treatment side effects</p>
<p>Child and family support</p>
<p>Explanations of chemotherapeutic reactions which may vary with specific drug regimen, the most side effects such as nausea and vomiting, body image changes e.g. alopecia and mucosal ulceration. Radiation effects may sometimes cause skin irritation and malaise</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pre-operative">Pre operative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-operative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Surgery done within 24-48 hours of diagnosis</p>
<p>Prepare parents for surgery; prepare all laboratory and operative procedures</p>
<p>Observations, monitor blood pressure (due to excess production of renin BP may be high)</p>
<p>34</p>
<p>Do not palpate the tumor unless when necessary since by doing so may cause dissemination of cancer cells to adjacent and distant sites</p>
<p>Radiotherapy and chemotherapy are almost done immediately, parents should be explained the benefits</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-operative">Post operative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-operative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nurse like any other abdominal surgery case; observe bowel movement, bowel sounds, distension and vomiting</p>
<p>Evaluate blood pressure frequently and observe for signs of infection</p>
<p>Hygiene measures to prevent infection</p>
<p>Support the family</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burkitt-s-lymphoma">Burkitt's lymphoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burkitt-s-lymphoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Burkitt lymphoma is a form of non Hodgkin's lymphoma in which cancer starts in immune cells called B-cells, recognized as the fastest growing human tumor. Burkitt lymphoma is associated with impaired immunity and is rapidly fatal if untreated, however intensive chemotherapy can achieve long term survival in more than half the people with Burkitt's</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Burkitts lymphoma is common in young children who also have malaria and Epstein Barr virus, allowing it to change infected B cells into cancerous cells. About 98% of African cases are associated with Epstein Barr infection. Outside Africa Burkitts lymphoma is especially likely to develop in people infected with HIV, the virus that causes AIDS, however incidences have reduced markedly since the introduction of high antiretroviral therapy (HAART)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types">Types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The world health organization (WHO), has categorized three types of burkitts lymphoma namely</p>
<ul>
<li>Endemic (African); Endemic Burkitts lymphoma primarily affects African children ages 4 to 7 and is twice as common in boys</li>
<li>Sporadic (non-African) occurs worldwide, globally it accounts for up to 40% of paediatric cases</li>
<li>Immunodeficiency- associated; this variant of burkitt's lymphoma is most common in people with HIV/AIDS. It can also occur in people with congenital conditions that cause immune deficiency and in organ transplant patients who take immunosuppressive drugs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-burkitts-lymphoma">Symptoms of Burkitts lymphoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-burkitts-lymphoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The symptoms depend with the type</p>
<ul>
<li>The endemic (African) variant, usually starts as tumors of the jaw or other facial bones, it can also affect the gastrointestinal tract, ovaries and breast and can spread to the central nervous system, causing nerve damage, weakness and paralysis</li>
<li>Sporadic and immunodeficiency-associated; usually start in the bowel and form a bulky tumor mass in the abdomen, often with massive involvement of liver, spleen and bone marrow. These variants can also start in the ovaries, testes, or other organs, and spread to the brain and spinal fluid</li>
</ul>
<p>Other symptoms associated with burkitt's lymphoma include</p>
<p>Loss of appetite, weight loss, fatigue, night sweets and unexplained fevers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Because burkitt's lymphoma spreads quickly, prompt diagnosis is essential</p>
<p>All or part of an enlarged lymph node or other suspicious disease, site will be biopsied and the sample examined under a microscope</p>
<p>Other tests include;</p>
<p>Computed tomography (CT) imaging of the abdomen, chest and pelvis</p>
<p>Chest x-ray</p>
<p>35</p>
<p>Bone marrow biopsy</p>
<p>Examination of the spinal fluid</p>
<p>Blood test to measure kidney and liver function</p>
<p>Testing for HIV disease</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Intensive intravenous chemotherapy which usually involves a hospital stay is the treatment for burkitt's lymphoma. Because burkitts lymphoma can spread to the CSF and spinal cord, chemotherapy drugs also may be injected directly into the cerebrospinal fluid, a treatment known as intrathecal chemotherapy.</p>
<p>Examples of drugs used include the following; cyclophosphamide, cytarabine, doxorubicin, etoposide, methotrexate, vincristine</p>
<p>Other treatments include Rituximab, a monoclonal antibody that sticks to proteins on cacer cells and stimulates the immune system to attack cancer cells</p>
<p>Autologus, stem cells transplantation, in which patients stem cells are removed and returned to the body</p>
<p>Radiation therapy</p>
<p>Steroid therapy</p>
<p>In some cases, surgery may be needed to remove parts of the intestine that are blocked, bleeding or have ruptured.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Burkitts lymphoma is fatal if left untreated in children; prompt intensive chemotherapy usually cures burkitts lymphoma, leading to prolong survival rates of 60% -90%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tetanus">Tetanus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def; Tetanus or lockjaw, is an acute, preventable disease caused by an exotoxin produced by the anaerobic, spore forming, gram-positive bacillus clostridium tetani. It is characterized by painful muscular rigidity primarily involving the masseter and neck muscles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The development of tetanus has four main requirements;</p>
<ul>
<li>Presence of tetanus spores or vegetative forms of the bacillus</li>
<li>Injury to the tissues</li>
<li>Wound conditions that encourage multiplication of the organism</li>
<li>A susceptible host</li>
</ul>
<p>Tetanus spores are found in soli, dust, and the intestinal tract of humans and animals. In newborn, infection may occur through the umbilical cord. In situations in which the infants are delivered in contaminated surroundings and mother has not been properly immunized against tetanus.</p>
<p>Incubation period- 3 days to 3 weeks</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When prevention efforts are not effective and conditions are favorable, the organisms multiply and form two exotoxins</p>
<p>Tetanospasmin, a potent toxin that affects the CNS to produce clinical manifestations of the disease</p>
<p>Tetanolysin, which appears to have no significance</p>
<p>The ideal conditions for growth of the organisms are devitalized (lack strength) tissues without access to air (e.g. puncture wound), wounds that have not been washed or kept clean and those that have crusted over, trapping pus inside. The exotoxin reaches the CNS by the way of either the neuron axons or the vascular</p>
<p>36</p>
<p>system. The toxin becomes fixed on the nerve cells of the brain stem and the anterior horn of the spinal cord. The toxin acts at the neuromuscular junction to produce muscular stiffness to lower the threshold for reflex excitability</p>
<p>NB: Shorter incubation periods have been associated with heavily contaminated wounds, more severe disease and a worse prognosis.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-f30357b5.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg">
Neonatal tetanus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Progressive stiffness and tenderness of muscles in the neck and jaw</p>
<p>Difficulty in opening the mouth (trismus) which is caused is caused by sustained contraction of the jaw- closing muscles</p>
<p>Spasms of facial muscles produce the so called sardonic smile (risus sardonicus)</p>
<p>Progressive involvement of the trunk muscles produce causes opisthotonus and a board like rigidity of the abdominal and limb muscles</p>
<p>Patient has difficult in swallowing and is highly sensitive to external stimuli. The slightest voice, a gentle touch, or bright light triggers convulsive muscular contractions that last seconds to minutes</p>
<p>The contractions reoccur with increased rate until they become almost continuous. Mental state is not affected, patient is alert, but in pain and distress which is reflected in a rapid pulse, sweating and an anxious expression.</p>
<p>Laryngospasm and tetany of respiratory muscles and accumulated secretions predispose the child to respiratory arrest and pneumonia. As the patient recovers from the disease the attacks become less frequent and gradually subside, complete recovery may take weeks</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Tetanus immunoglobulin to neutralize the toxins</p>
<p>Antibiotics- penicillin or erythromycin</p>
<p>Best treated at an intensive care facility, where close and constant observations and equipment for monitoring are available</p>
<p>Diazepam is the drug of choice for seizure control and muscle relaxation</p>
<p>Other muscle relaxants can be used e.g. baclofen</p>
<p>Neuromuscular blocking drugs g vecuronium- has paralytic effect on respiratory muscles, and so use of these drugs requires mechanical ventilation with endotracheal intubation</p>
<p>Administer analgesics</p>
<p>Maintain airway</p>
<p>Fluid and electrolyte balance and ensuring adequate fluid intake</p>
<p>Maintain a dark quiet room and minimize touch; however the lighting should be enough so as to observe the patient well.</p>
<p>Prevent complications associated with prolonged immobility, deceased bowel and bladder tone and subsequent constipation, anorexia, DVT, pneumonia and skin breakdown</p>
<p>Parents/patient need support, information and reassurance from the nurse</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus toxoid to all ANC mothers</li>
<li>Keep wounds clean/ receive T.T booster</li>
<li>During delivery minimize contamination during and after delivery and the umbilical stump, avoid applying local concoctions on the baby’s umbilical stump</li>
<li>Proper surgical debridement and cleaning of contaminated wounds to reduce the chance of infection</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="congenital-anomalies">Congenital Anomalies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-anomalies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="congenital-anomalies-of-gi-tract">Congenital Anomalies of GI tract<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-anomalies-of-gi-tract" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="cleft-palate-and-cleft-lip">Cleft palate and cleft lip<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleft-palate-and-cleft-lip" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>A cleft lip contains an opening in the upper lip that may extend into the nose. The opening may be on one side, both side or in the middle.</p>
<p>Cleft palate is a congenital split in the roof of the mouth.</p>
<p>Together, these birth defects are commonly called ‘orofacial clefts’</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>The causes include;</li>
<li>Problems with genes passed down from one or both parents, drugs, viruses or other toxins</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>The upper lip is derived from medial nasal and maxillary processes, failure of merging between the medial nasal and maxillary processes at five weeks’ gestation, on one or both sides, results to cleft lip. CL usually occurs at the junction between the central and lateral parts of the upper lip on either side.</p>
<p>Cleft palate is a partial or lack of fusion of palatial shelves, and it occurs in numerous ways</p>
<ul>
<li>Defective growth of palatal shelves</li>
<li>Failure of the shelves to attain a horizontal position</li>
<li>Lack of contact shelves</li>
<li>Rupture after fusion of shelves</li>
</ul>
<p>Fusion of palatial shelves begins at 8 weeks’ and continuous usually until 12 weeks’ gestation. One hypothesis is that a threshold is need beyond which delayed movement of palatial shelves does not allow closure to take place, and result in a cleft palate</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Genetic and environmental factor; in those instances, genetic factors create susceptibility for clefts. When environmental factors (i.e. triggers) interact with a genetically susceptible genotype, a cleft palate develops during an early stage of development.</p>
<p>38</p>
<p>Images of cleft lip and cleft palate</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-3c9f061c.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
A</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-20917e93.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>

<p>A. Lateral cleft lip B. Bilateral cleft lip C. Cleft palate D. Middle line lip</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Management require coordinated care provider in many fields of medicine and include the following; otolaryngology, dentistry, speech pathology, genetics, nursing, mental health and social medicine. Care is specialized and costly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-therapy">Medical therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="neonatal-care">Neonatal care.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neonatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Major concerns include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Risk of aspiration, because of the communication between oral and nasal cavities</li>
<li>Airway obstruction</li>
</ul>
<p>39</p>
<ul>
<li>Difficult with feeding of a child with a cleft and nasal regurgitation</li>
</ul>
<p>Hints of feeding breast milk with a bottle are as follows;</p>
<p>Particularly for infants with cleft palate breastfeeding is not possible, and so the mother can express EBM</p>
<p>Various nipples and bottles are made specifically for infants with clefts; the goal is to find a nipple and bottle that makes feeding easy for the infant and still allow ample opportunity to suck.</p>
<p>A soft nipple is generally than a hard nipple, use a cross cut nipple to prevent choking; any nipple can be cross cut manually by using a single-edged razor blade; the cross cut is on the tongue side. The bottle should be squeezed and released, not continually squeezed</p>
<p>The nipple is angled to a side of the mouth, away from the cleft.</p>
<p>More upright or seated positions prevent the milk from leaking to the nose and causing the infant to choke</p>
<p>Advice the mother to stop feeding and allow the infant to cough or sneeze for a few seconds when nasal regurgitation occurs; palatal obturator may be used</p>
<p>Gaining weight and preventing aspiration and ear infections are the most important parts of caring for neonates with a cleft during their first days and weeks of life</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgery-therapy">Surgery therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgery-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rule of 10s- weight 10 lb, 10 g/dl of hemoglobin and 10 weeks of age however pediatricians are presently more flexible and some surgeons may well justify a neonatal lip closure, considering the rule 3 10s is still very useful</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Preconception supplementation of folic acid and multivitamins especially in those situations which environmental factors represent a substantial part of the etiological background</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="esophageal-atresia-and-tracheoesophageal-fistula">Esophageal atresia and Tracheoesophageal fistula.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#esophageal-atresia-and-tracheoesophageal-fistula" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Esophageal atresia is when the esophagus terminates before it reaches the stomach, ending in a blind pouch while tracheoesophageal fistula is a communication of esophagus and trachea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Esophageal atresia or/and tracheoesophageal fistula, results either from spontaneous posterior deviation of the tracheoesophageal septum or from mechanical factor pushing the dorsal wall of the foregut anteriorly. In its most forms the upper part of the esophagus end as a blind sac and the lower part of the esophagus end as a blind sac and the lower part is connected to the trachea by narrow canal just above the bifurcation. Atresia of the esophagus prevents normal passage of amniotic fluid into the intestinal tract, resulting in accumulation of excess fluid in the amniotic sac (polyhydraminos)</p>
<p>40</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-94a3bf8a.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg">
Atresia with distal fistula (86%)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-7088dfef.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg">
Isolated esophageal atresia (8%)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-34024bf3.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg">
Atresia with double fistula (1%)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-400fa272.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg">
Isolated tracheoesophageal fistula (H type) (4%)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-197a3030.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
Atresia with proximal fistula (1%)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Choking, coughing and sneezing</li>
<li>Infant swallows normally but begins to cough and struggle as the fluid returns through nose and mouth.</li>
<li>Infant may become cyanotic due to lack of oxygen and may stop breathing as the overflow of fluid from the blind pouch is aspirated into trachea.</li>
<li>Respiratory distress</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prenatal: Ultrasonography
Postnatal: NGT or orogastric tube placement and x-ray</li>
</ul>
<p>Routine prenatal ultrasonography may suggest esophageal atresia. Polyhydramnios may be present but is not diagnostic because it can occur with many other disorders.</p>
<p>After delivery, an NGT or an orogastric tube is inserted if esophageal atresia is suspected by prenatal ultrasonography or clinical findings; diagnosis of esophageal atresia is suggested by inability to pass the tube into the stomach. A radiopaque catheter determines the location of the atresia on x-ray.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgical repair</li>
</ul>
