<p>Preoperative management aims to get the infant into optimal condition for surgery and prevent aspiration pneumonia, which makes surgical correction more hazardous. Oral feedings are withheld. Continuous suction with an NGT in the upper esophageal pouch prevents aspiration of swallowed saliva. The infant should be positioned prone with the head elevated 30 to 40° and with the right side down to facilitate gastric emptying and minimize the risk of aspirating gastric acid through the fistula. If definitive repair must be deferred because of extreme prematurity, aspiration pneumonia, or other congenital malformations, a gastrostomy tube is placed to decompress the stomach. Suction through the gastrostomy tube then reduces the risk that gastric contents will reflux through the fistula into the tracheobronchial tree.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypertrophic-pyloric-stenosis">Hypertrophic pyloric stenosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypertrophic-pyloric-stenosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Also referred to as infantile hypertrophic pyloric stenosis, hypertrophic pyloric stenosis occurs when the circular muscle of the pyloric sphincter becomes thickened, resulting in elongation and narrowing of the pyloric canal, this results to outlet obstruction and compensatory dilatation, hypertrophy and hyperperistalsis of the stomach. This condition develops in the first few weeks of life causing projectile vomiting, dehydration, metabolic alkalosis and failure to thrive</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidemiology">Epidemiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Incidence: 1:300-500 live births.</li>
<li>Male to female ratio = 4:1</li>
<li>Classically presents in a 1st born male between 3-6 weeks of age.</li>
<li>Causes: familial link</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Caused by diffuse hypertrophy and hyperplasia of the smooth muscle of the antrum of the stomach and pylorus. It is postulated that this abnormal innervation of the muscular layer leads to failure of relaxation of the pyloric muscle, increased synthesis of growth factors, and subsequent hypertrophy, hyperplasia, and obstruction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Non bilious vomiting</li>
<li>Projectile vomiting increasingly</li>
<li>Child has voracious appetite</li>
<li>Dehydration due to vomiting</li>
<li>Less flatus passage</li>
<li>Fewer stool/constipation</li>
<li>Hypochloremic, hypokalemic metabolic alkalosis</li>
<li>Typical "olive" mass in RUQ on palpation</li>
<li>Visible gastric (peristalsis) waves moving from left to right in upper abdomen</li>
<li>Failure to gain weight &amp; lethargy: most babies with this condition will fail to gain weight.</li>
</ul>
<p>42</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperbilirubinemia: Starvation can exacerbate diminished hepatic glucoronyl transferase activity, and indirect hyperbilirubinemia may be seen in 1-2% of affected infants.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Initially suggested by the typical clinical presentation</p>
<p>Physical examination: The mass is firm, mobile, approximately 2 cm, best palpated from the left, located in the midepigastrium beneath the liver edge.</p>
<p>Palpation of the hard muscle mass or olive is diagnostic in conjunction with a typical history.</p>
<p>Ultrasonography is used to measure the thickness of the pyloric wall and the length of the pyloric canal. It is reliable and easily performed and has become the main investigation</p>
<p>Upper GI barium studies is cost-effective than ultrasound and can identify other possible diagnoses such as GERD.</p>
<p>Serum electrolytes (for correction of imbalances before surgical repair) there is often metabolic alkalosis with severe K+ depletion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fluid resuscitation - Fluid therapy should be continued until the infant is rehydrated</p>
<p>Correct electrolyte imbalance - acid-base, and electrolyte losses.</p>
<p>Stop feeding and do a stomach wash out to reduce edema of stomach wall</p>
<p>Intravenous fluid therapy is begun with 0.45–0.9% saline, in 5–10% dextrose, with the addition of potassium chloride in concentrations.</p>
<p>Fluid therapy should be continued until the infant is rehydrated and the serum bicarbonate concentration is less than 30 mEq/dL, which implies that the alkalosis has been corrected.</p>
<p>Most infants can be rehydrated within 24 hours</p>
<p>Surgery - Fredet-Ramstedt pyloromyotomy: In this procedure the thickened muscles of the pylorus are divided along the length of pylorus till the mucosa is seen.</p>
<p>After surgery, the baby can be fed after 18-24 hours with small quantity of clear fluids and increase gradually if patients tolerate.</p>
<p>Withhold feeds in case of vomiting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-postoperative-complications">Common postoperative complications.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-postoperative-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Vomiting due to incomplete myotomy</li>
<li>Perforation of the pyloric mucosa</li>
<li>Hemorrhage</li>
<li>Wound infection.</li>
<li>Surface mucous producing cell hyperplasia which causes persistent gastric outlet obstruction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="danger-signs-for-pyloric-stenosis-post-surgery">Danger signs for pyloric stenosis post surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#danger-signs-for-pyloric-stenosis-post-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent or projectile vomiting after feeding</li>
<li>Poor weight gain or weight loss</li>
<li>Decreased activity or lethargy</li>
<li>Few or no stools over a period of 1 or 2 days</li>
<li>Signs of dehydration such as decreased urination (more than 4-6 hours between wet diapers)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Excellent unless diagnosis is delayed and prolonged severe dehydration occurs.</li>
<li>Mortality is rare after pyloromyotomy.</li>
</ul>
<p>43</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abdominal-wall-defects">ABDOMINAL WALL DEFECTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abdominal-wall-defects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ompalocele">Ompalocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ompalocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Omphalocele involves herniation of abdominal viscera through an enlarged umbilical ring. The viscera which may include liver small and large intestines, stomach, spleen or gall bladder are covered by amnion, Wharton's jelly and peritoneum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The origin of the defect is a failure of the bowel to return to the body cavity from its physiological herniation during the  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>6</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">6^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>10</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  weeks</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="epidemiology">Epidemiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Omphalocele occurs in 2.5/10,000 births and is associated with a high mortality rate and severe malformations such as cardiac anomalies and neural tube defects. Approximately  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>15</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">15\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">15%</span></span></span></span></span>  of live-born infants with omphalocele have chromosomal abnormalities</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-2736cb95.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p>Note the membrane covering the abdominal contents in this omphalocele</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Vital signs</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain body temperature</li>
<li>Cover with saline-soaked gauze and trunk wrap circumferentially.
Prophylactic antibiotics if ruptures
Large defects  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex-error" title="ParseError: KaTeX parse error: Expected 'EOF', got '&amp;' at position 1: &amp;̲gt;7" style="color: rgb(204, 0, 0);">&amp;gt;7</span></span>  cm in diameter treat with desiccating substances e.g povidone-iodine, silver sulfadiazine e.t.c.</li>
<li>Takes 2-3 months before re-epithelialization occurs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gastroschisis">Gastroschisis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gastroschisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Gastroschisis is the term applied to a protrusion of abdominal contents through the body wall. It occurs lateral to the umbilicus usually on the right, and the defect is most likely due to abnormal closure of the body wall. Viscera are not covered by peritoneum or amnion, and the bowel may be damaged by exposure to amniotic fluid. Size of defect much smaller (&lt; 4 cm) than omphalocele</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-cff2ca95.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="epidemiology">Epidemiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Gastrochisis occurs in 1/10,000 births but is increasing in frequency, especially among young women (&lt; 20 years old) and the reason for this increase is not known. Gastrochisis is not associated with chromosomal abnormalities or other severe defects</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Need urgent surgical intervention</li>
<li>Surgical closure</li>
<li>Plastic spring-waded silo can be placed onto the bowel and secured beneath the fascia.</li>
<li>The silo covers the bowel and allows for graduated reduction on a daily basis as the edema in the bowel wall decreases.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prenatal-management">PRENATAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prenatal-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Maternal serum alpha-fetoprotein</li>
<li>Maternal ultrasonography (look for other abnormalities)
Counseling on prognosis</li>
<li>Transfer to a centre where the newborn can be managed best.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postnatal-management">POSTNATAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postnatal-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>GENERAL CARE.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Manage in nursery in an incubator or under over head warmer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pass nasogastric tube to decompress the stomach and prevent aspiration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Start fluid resuscitation and slightly higher volumes are required.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ventilatory support in case of respiratory distress.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Urinary catheter to measure the urinary output.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Omphalocele with an intact sac, cover and support it with sterile dry gauze dressing.
Omphalocele with a ruptured sac or gastroschisis, cover contents with wet sterile gauze dressing to prevent drying of the contents.
Nurse child on-side to prevent damage or vascular compromise due to drag on the vascular pedicle.
Cover lower body including defect in a sterile transparent plastic bag to prevent hypothermia and evaporative water loss while permitting inspection of the contents.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definitive-treatment">Definitive treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitive-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Operative treatment – aim of surgery is to replace the exposed viscera into the abdominal cavity and provide cover with the abdominal wall.
Only skin may be closed creating a ventral hernia, or a silo made of artificial material may be put, which is reduced later for closure of the abdomen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-operative-treatment">Non operative treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-operative-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Carried out when severe congenital malformations preclude definitive surgery or omphalocele too large for the surgical procedure to be successful.
Paint the sac with mercurochrome or silver nitrate to promote epithelization and formation of ventral hernia which can be repaired later.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="df284b76">Hirschsprung’s disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#df284b76" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hirschsprung’s disease also known as congenital megacolon is due to an absence of parasympathetic ganglia in the bowel wall (agangionic megacolon), together with hypertrophy of the nerve trunks.
Results from failure of neuroblasts into the gut from vagal nerve trunks at the end of the 1st trimester of fetal life HD is characterized by the absence of myenteric and submucosal ganglion cells (Auerbach and Meissner plexuses) along a variable length of the distal gastrointestinal tract.
The disease results in decreased motility in the affected bowel segment, lack of propagation of peristaltic waves into the aganglionic colon, and abnormal or absent relaxation of this segment and of the internal anal sphincter.
2/3 of patients, the rectum and lower sigmoid colon are involved.
Absence of ganglion cells gives rise to a contracted non-peristaltic segment with a dilated hypertrophied segment of normal colon above it, due to absence of the nerve supply in the distal part of the colon.
Due to the absence of the ganglion cells in the affected gut, peristaltic waves are deficient and the proximal large intestine becomes dilated and distended.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidemiology">Epidemiology.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs in about 1:4500 live births.</li>
<li>Shows a familial tendency</li>
<li>More common in males than in females</li>
<li>Associated with Down syndrome in 10% of patients.</li>
</ul>
<p>46</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-f51e3bb2.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
Figure: A barium enema showing a "long segment" Hirschsprung's disease. The transition zone is in the transverse colon. The arrow demonstrates the area of the transition zone between the enlarged area which has ganglion cells (normal) and the small area which does not (Hirschsprung's disease).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classically-the-bowel-just-before-the-segment-with-hirschsprung-s-disease-becomes-distended-and-enlarged-this-distended-bowel-has-ganglion-cells-the-characteristic-problem-in-the-bowel-with-hirschsprung-s-is-the-absence-of-ganglion-cells">Classically the bowel just before the segment with Hirschsprung's disease becomes distended and enlarged. This distended bowel has ganglion cells. The characteristic problem in the bowel with Hirschsprung's is the absence of ganglion cells.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classically-the-bowel-just-before-the-segment-with-hirschsprung-s-disease-becomes-distended-and-enlarged-this-distended-bowel-has-ganglion-cells-the-characteristic-problem-in-the-bowel-with-hirschsprung-s-is-the-absence-of-ganglion-cells" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The aganglionic segment almost always includes the rectum and proximal portion of the large intestine.</p>
<p>Lack of innervation produces the functional defect that results in absence of propulsive movements (peristalsis) that causes accumulation of intestinal contents and distension of the bowel proximal to the defect (megacolon).</p>
<p>Failure of the internal anal sphincter to relax contributes to the clinical manifestation of obstruction because it prevents evacuation of solids, liquids and gas.</p>
<p>Intestinal distention and ischemia may occur as a result of distention of the bowel wall, which contributes to the development of enterocolitis, the leading cause of death in children with Hirschsprung disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In Newborns presents as delayed passage of meconium or acute intestinal obstruction with or without infection i.e. enterocolitis</p>
<p>Neonate fails to pass meconium for more than 48 hours and develops distension of abdomen and bilious vomiting.</p>
<p>In old age, the child may present as chronic constipation and abdominal distension.</p>
<p>Failure to thrive and the child looks malnourished.</p>
<p>O/E, the abdomen is distended with visible loops or palpable fecaloma, severe constipation</p>
<p>Rectal examination shows empty rectum and withdrawal of fingers results in passage of stool.</p>
<p>Delayed passage of meconium  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex-error" title="ParseError: KaTeX parse error: Expected 'EOF', got '&amp;' at position 2: (&amp;̲gt;24\mathrm{h}" style="color: rgb(204, 0, 0);">(&amp;gt;24\mathrm{h}</span></span>  after birth)</p>
<p>Abdominal distension that is relieved by rectal stimulation or enemas</p>
<p>Vomiting</p>
<p>Neonatal enterocolitis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="older-children-and-adult-symptoms-are-as-follows">Older children and adult symptoms are as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#older-children-and-adult-symptoms-are-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Chronic abdominal distension</p>
<p>Classification;</p>
<p>Patients can be classified by the extension of the aganglionosis, as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Classic short-segment HD (75% of cases) - Aganglionic segment does not extend beyond the upper sigmoid
Long-segment HD (20% of cases)
Total colonic aganglionosis (3-12% of cases)</li>
</ul>
<p>Investigations</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Plain X-ray of the abdomen reveal air fluid levels in cases presenting with intestinal obstruction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rectal contrast studies (barium enema) demonstrate the transition zone in the recto sigmoid colon with retained barium even after 24 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rectal biopsy is taken from the rectum to confirm the diagnosis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arorectal pressure measurement is very helpful in diagnosis.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Includes rehydration, systemic antibiotics, nasogastric decompression and rectal irrigation while diagnosis is being confirmed</p>
<p>Depends on age of patient, length of involved segment, severity of symptoms and presence of enterocolitis With presenting enterocolitis, an initial colostomy is performed low in the ganglionated segment.</p>
<p>Child with constipation alone, dilated intestine can be evacuated with repeat rectal saline washouts and enema as a first step.</p>
<p>In neonates definitive operation is delayed until the weighs 10kgs (10 months – 1 year)</p>
<p>Aims at removal of aganglionic segment of bowel and restoring the continuity of the gut.</p>
<p>Done in 2 or 3 stages.</p>
<p>Nursing considerations</p>
<p>Record the time of first passage of meconium.</p>
<p>If diagnostic barium enema is planned, it is essential to avoid preparatory rectal wash. This distorts the anatomy of the rectosigmoid region and transition zone may be missed.</p>
<p>Daily rectal washes should be given to the child if primary pull through is planned or there is delay in the colostomy.</p>
<p>Rectal wash is done with normal saline.</p>
<p>Antibiotics and fluid should be given as per instructions.</p>
<p>Rectal manipulations are kept to a minimum as these may cause rectal injury.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anal-rectal-malformations">Anal rectal malformations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anal-rectal-malformations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These malformations may range from simple imperforated anus to include other associated complex anomalies of GU and pelvic organs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classifications">Classifications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classifications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="male">Male<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Perineal fistula</p>
<p>Rectal urethral bulbar fistula</p>
<p>Rectal urethral prostatic fistula</p>
<p>Rectal vesicular (bladder neck) fistula</p>
<p>Imperforate bladder without fistula</p>
<p>Rectal atresia and stenosis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="female">Female<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Perineal fistula</p>
<p>Vestibular fistula</p>
<p>Imperforate anus without fistula</p>
<p>Rectal atresia stenosis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cloaca">Cloaca<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cloaca" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Rectal atresia occur when the anal opening appears normal, there is a midline intergluteal groove and usually no fistula exist between the rectum and urinary tract.</p>
<p>Rectal atresia is a complete obstruction (inability to pass stool) and requires immediate surgical intervention</p>
<p>Rectal stenosis presents later in infancy when the infant has a history of difficulty stooling, abdominal distension, and ribbon like stools</p>
<p>48</p>
<p>A persistent cloaca is a complex anorectal malformation in which the rectum, vagina and urethra drain into a common channel opening into the opening</p>
<p>Imperforate anus includes several forms of malformation without obvious opening</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During embryonic development the cloaca (end of the digestive tract) becomes the common channel for the developing urinary, genital and rectal systems. The cloaca is divided at the six week of gestation into an anterior urogenital sinus and a posterior intestinal channel by the urorectal septum. After the lateral folds joins the urorectal septum, separation of the urinary and rectal segment takes place. Further differentiation results in the anterior GU system and the posterior and rectal channel. An interruption of this development leads to incomplete migration of the rectum to its normal perineal position</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Physical finding of an absent anal opening, abdominal distension, vomiting, absence of meconium passage or presence of meconium in urine</p>
<p>A flat perineum with the absence of a midline intergluteal groove</p>
<p>In anal fistula a prominent anal dimple and a band of skin tissue is seen commonly called a 'bucket handle'</p>
<p>Abdominal and pelvic ultrasonography</p>
<p>An IV pyelogram and voiding cystourethrogram</p>
<p>Pelvic MRI, radiography, ultrasound and fluoroscopic examination of the pelvis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Surgery</p>
<p>Stabilise the newborn and keep NPO</p>
<p>Give IVF's</p>
<p>Nursing</p>
<p>Responsibility is assisting in identification of anal rectal malformations. A newborn that does not pass stools in the first 24 hours nor has meconium that appears at a location other than the anal opening requires further assessment</p>
<p>Family support depending on the operation carried out and advice on discharge about home care of the baby which includes bowel irrigation programs, toilet training, stool softeners use and diet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="congenital-neurologic-anomalies">Congenital Neurologic Anomalies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-neurologic-anomalies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hydrocephalus">Hydrocephalus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hydrocephalus is accumulation of excessive amounts of CSF, causing cerebral ventricular enlargement and/or increased intracranial pressure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Congenital (myelomeningocele, intrauterine viral infection- cytomegalovirus, toxoplasmosis)</p>
<p>Aqueduct stenosis</p>
<p>Acquired conditions such as intraventricular hemorrhage, tumor, CSF infections or head injury</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CSF is circulated throughout the ventricular system and is then absorbed within the arachnoid spaces by a mechanism that is not entirely clear. 1. Impaired absorption of CSF fluid within the subarachnoid space, damage of the subarachnoid cisterns or malfunction of arachnoid villi leads to nonobstructive or communicating hydrocephalus. 2. Obstruction of the flow of CSF through the ventricular system leads to obstructive or noncommunicating hrocephalous. Myelomeningocele is characterized by herniation of a small cerebellum,</p>
<p>49</p>
<p>medulla,pons and fourth ventrical into the cervical canal through an enlarged foramen magnum, and the resulting obstruction cause hydrocephalus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Communicating hydrocephalus (non obstructive)
Caused by impaired CSF reabsorption within the subarachnoid space. There is no obstruction of CSF between ventricles and subarachnoid space.</li>
<li>Non communicating (obstructive) Caused by CSF flow obstruction in ventricles.</li>
<li>Congenital</li>
<li>Acquired: Due to CNS infections like meningitis, brain tumors, head trauma, intracranial hemorrhage.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-and-signs">Symptoms and Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-and-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Neurologic findings depend on whether intracranial pressure is increased, symptoms of which in infants include irritability, high-pitched cry, vomiting, lethargy, strabismus, and bulging fontanelle. Older, verbal children may complain of headache, decreased vision, or both. Papilloedema is a late sign of increased intracranial pressure; its initial absence does not exclude hydrocephalus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prenatal ultrasonography</li>
<li>Neonates: Cranial ultrasonography</li>
<li>Older infants and children: CT or MRI</li>
<li>After birth, diagnosis is suspected if routine examination reveals an increased head circumference; infants may have a bulging fontanelle or widely separated cranial sutures.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sometimes observation or serial lumbar punctures</li>
<li>For severe cases, a ventricular shunt procedure</li>
</ul>
<p>Progressive hydrocephalus usually requires a ventricular shunt. Shunts typically connect the right lateral ventricle to the peritoneal cavity</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="shunt-complications">Shunt complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shunt-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Malfunction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-points">Key Points<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-points" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hydrocephalus is usually caused by obstruction to the normal flow of CSF but can be due to impaired resorption of CSF.</li>
<li>If the disorder occurs before the cranial sutures have fused, the head may be enlarged, with bulging fontanelles.</li>
<li>Neurologic symptoms develop mainly if intracranial pressure increases; infants may have irritability, high-pitched cry, vomiting, lethargy, and strabismus.</li>
<li>Diagnose using ultrasonography prenatally and in neonates; use MRI or CT for older children.</li>
<li>Treat with observation or serial lumbar punctures or a ventricular shunt procedure depending on the etiology and severity and progression of symptoms.</li>
</ul>
<p>50</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spinal-bifida">Spinal Bifida<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-bifida" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Spinal bifida is defective closure of the vertebral column.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Although the cause is not known, low folate levels during pregnancy increase risk. There seems to be a genetic component. Other risk factors include maternal use of certain drugs (eg, valproate) and maternal diabetes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types">Types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>-Spinal bifida occulta which refers to a defect that is not visible externally</p>
<p>-Spinal bifida cystic which refers to a visible defect with an external sac like and the two major forms include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Meningocele which encases meninges and spinal fluid, but no neural elements
Myelomeningocele(or meningomyelocele), which contains meninges, spinal fluid and nerves</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-088cd4ce.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-2acbaaa4.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Primarily defect in neural tube malformations is a failure of neural tubal closure; however some evidence indicates that the defects are as a result of splitting of the already closed neural tube as a result of abnormal increase in CSF pressure during the first trimester</p>
<p>52</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms-and-signs">Symptoms and Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-and-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many children with minor defects are asymptomatic.</p>
<p><strong>Neurologic</strong>: Paralysis and sensory deficits are present below the lesion. Rectal tone is usually decreased.</p>
<p><strong>Hydrocephalus</strong></p>
<p><strong>Orthopedic</strong>: Lack of muscle innervation leads to atrophy of the legs.</p>
<p><strong>Urologic</strong>: Paralysis also impairs bladder function, occasionally leading to a neurogenic bladder and, consequently, urinary reflux, which can cause hydronephrosis, frequent UTIs, and, ultimately, kidney damage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ultrasonography or MRI</li>
<li>Prenatal screening can be done by doing fetal ultrasonography and by measuring maternal serum levels of α-fetoprotein</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgical repair of the spinal lesion</li>
<li>Sometimes a ventricular shunt</li>
<li>Various measures for orthopedic and urologic complications</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Folate supplementation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-sex-development">Disorders of sex development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-sex-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ambiguous-genitalia">Ambiguous genitalia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ambiguous-genitalia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ambiguous genitalia are birth defect where the outer genitals don't have the typical appearance of either a boy or girl.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Abnormalities of chromosome, defects of embryogenesis, or biochemical (hormonal) abnormalities, disturbances in any of these leads to abnormal development resulting to ambiguous genitalia</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="stages-of-normal-development">Stages of normal development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-normal-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>For the first six weeks of life the developing embryo is morphologically asexual, neither male nor female. The primitive bipotential (able to form testicle or an ovary) gonad consist of an outer layer (the cortex) and the inner medulla.</p>
<p>Differentiation into testes or ovaries takes place during the seventh and the eighth weeks of gestation. At this time the medullary portion develops and the cortical zone regresses. In female the cortical zone is preserved while the medullary regresses</p>
<p>Active factors cause the mullerian duct system to regress and without these factors the primitive gonad has a tendency to feminize. The embryonic ovary develops in the absence of male hormone stimulation.</p>
<p>The final stage of genital and reproductive organ development is differentiation of the external genitalia, which in the early consist of urogenital sinus, two lateral scrotal swelling and an anteriorly situated genital tubercle.</p>
<p>Depending on the presence or absence of male hormones the genital tubercle differentiates into a penis or a clitoris. In response to testicular androgens, labosacral folds fuse to form a scrotum and the ventral skin of the penis; the urethral fold form the perineal and penile urethra, without the influence of masculinizing secretions, the urethral folds do not fuse and instead become labia minora, the labia sacral folds remain fused to separate</p>
<p>into labia majora and the urogenital sinus differentiates into a lower vagina and the vagina and urethral openings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="abnormal-genitalia-and-reproductive-organ-development">Abnormal genitalia and reproductive organ development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abnormal-genitalia-and-reproductive-organ-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disturbances of normal order of events in gender determination produce abnormal genitalia and reproductive organ development with the presence of ambiguous or indeterminate external genitalia at birth. Ambiguous genitalia can be variable and can conform to one gender or other. In some, external sexual structures represent those of normal male or female, where as the karyotype is the direct opposite. situation in which the phenotypic gender differs from chromosome gender is a disorder of sex development. A failure or abnormality in any of the four steps of genital and reproductive organ development can lead to abnormal development in subsequent stages. The mechanisms and sites of defective development include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Abnormal gender determination- chromosome abnormalities result in disturbance of secondary sexual characteristics and reproductive organ development.</li>
<li>Abnormal differentiation of gonads- when induction of the bipotential gonad fails, gender differentiation proceeds in the direction of the female phenotype, regardless of the karyotype.</li>
<li>Abnormal differentiation of ductal systems-Biological inactivity of androgenic male organizer substances or insensitivity of ductal tissue to the action of these substances, result in a persistent female duct system, which leads to the presence of uterus and uterine tubes</li>
<li>Abnormal secretion of or tissue insensitivity to testicular androgen- complete failure of male hormones secretion produces female external genitalia in a genetic male.. Partial or incomplete failure results in incomplete masculinization with ambiguity of the external genitalia. The female genital fetus exposed into large amounts of andrenogenic hormone may exhibit varying degrees of masculinization of the external genitalia (congenital andrenal hyperplasia)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-abnormalities">Types of abnormalities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-abnormalities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some disorders with abnormal genital development are not characterized by ambiguous genitalia in the newborn period. e.g. the most common chromosome disorders do not become apparent until later in childhood, adolescence and adulthood when the individual seeks medical attention because of delayed development and infertility</p>
<p>The four conditions of producing ambiguous genitalia in the newborn that require prompt and accurate evaluation are the:</p>
<ul>
<li>The masculinized female</li>
<li>The incompletely masculinized male</li>
<li>The presence of both male and female sex organs</li>
<li>Mixed gonad dysgenisis</li>
</ul>
<p>An ambiguous genitalia in the newborn is often as a result of the virilization in the female by adrenal androgens after the time of early gonadal differentiation. The most common type is congenital adrenogenital hyperplasia, which is an inherited deficiency of adrenal corticoid hormones. Due to decreased cortisol the pituitary gland is stimulated and produces ACTH which causes the adrenal cortex to increase the production of adrenal hormones, including the androgens, because the adrenal gland differentiates later than the gonadal duct system, but before differentiation of the external genitalia, masculization of the external genitalia is the prominent feature. The internal female anatomy is normal.</p>
<p>The external genitalia in the incompletely masculinized male may be incompletely male, ambiguous or completely female. Defects may be as a result of deficient production of fetal androgen, deficiency in any of the enzymes needed testosterone biosynthesis, or unresponsiveness or subresponsiveness of genital structures to testosterone. Individuals who may be either genetic males or females with both ovarian and testicular tissues with an ovary on one side and a testis on the other or a combination of ovotestis, are rare. The external genitalia may be a male (possibly cryptorchid with a micro penis) or normal female, but are ambiguous in the majority of cases</p>
<p>53</p>
<p>Mixed gonadol dysgenesis, in which the affected infants are sex chromosome mosaics (an individual with varying cell composition). Genitalia vary greatly, but in those who appear predominantly, the dysplastic testis may cause masculinization at puberty.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>History- previous miscarriages (may help identify chromosome which deviated from normal) maternal ingestion of steroids, relatives with disorders of sex development or unplanned death in the first weeks of live, maternal ovarian tumor in pregnancy</p>
<p>Physical examination- presence of gonads strongly suggestive a male genotype, uterus palpable by rectal examination, length of penis stretched to measure location of urethral orifice, location of vagina orifice. Prader staging to determine degree of virilization of external genitalia</p>
<p>Chromosome analysis- chromosome abnormalities and precise genetic picture of a person chromosome (karyotype) DNA analysis</p>
<p>Endoscopic, ultrasonography and radiographic contrast media studies, presence or absence or nature of internal genital and urinary structures</p>
<p>Biochemical test- include urinary steroid secretions to help detect several of the andrenocortical syndromes (congenital adrenogenital hyperplasia)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ambiguous-findings">Ambiguous findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ambiguous-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Micro penis (2.5-3 cm) in newborn, maybe enlarged clitoris</p>
<p>Urethral meatus anywhere along dorsal or ventral surface of penis, especially on perineum</p>
<p>Small scrotum with smooth, tight skin and any degree of separation in midline may be enlarged labia</p>
<p>Absent testes, may be undescended, if combined with small scrotum, may be evidence of enlarged labia</p>
<p>Enlarged clitoris that protrudes from labia, may suggest small penis</p>
<p>Urethral meatus located in clitoris, may suggest small penis</p>
<p>Prominent labia, partially or completely fused with palpable masses on each side, may be small scrotum with testis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The overall goal of management is to enable the affected child to grow into a well-adjusted, psychologically stable person, who is able to identify with the assigned gender and is content with the same</p>
<p>Gender identity should be established by two and half years</p>
<p>Females with congenital adrenogenital hyperplasia or virilization are treated with steroids and surgical intervention</p>
<p>Males with hpospadias and crytorchidism (under virilization) may be successfully reared males and surgical repair done</p>
<p>The child with mixed gonadal dysgenesis may be assigned gender on phallus and androgen exposure</p>
<p>Male infants with micro penis may respond to testosterone and be successfully reared as boys</p>
<p>Nursing</p>
<p>Family needs a great deal of support, and encouragement from nurses, and the health care team to cope with the emotionally charged situation, parents are confused, anxious, and overwhelmed by feeling of guilt and shame.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assignment">Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Epispadias</li>
<li>Hypospadias</li>
<li>Phimosis and paraphimosis</li>
<li>Cryptorchidism (Undescended Testes)</li>
</ul>
<p>54</p>
<p>55</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="convulsive-disorders">Convulsive disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#convulsive-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A seizure is an abnormal, unregulated electrical discharge that occurs within the brain’s cortical gray matter and transiently interrupts normal brain function.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Common causes of seizures vary by age of onset:</p>
<ul>
<li>Before age 2: Fever, birth or developmental defects, birth injuries, and metabolic disorders</li>
<li>Ages 2 to 14: Idiopathic seizure disorders</li>
<li>Adults: Cerebral trauma, alcohol withdrawal, tumors, strokes, and an unknown cause (in 50%)</li>
<li>The elderly: Tumors and strokes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Seizures are classified as <strong>generalized</strong> or <strong>partial</strong>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-generalized">1.
