Generalized<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-generalized" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In generalized seizures, the abnormal electrical discharge diffusely involves the entire cortex of both hemispheres from the onset, and consciousness is usually lost.</p>
<p>Generalized seizures include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infantile spasms</li>
<li>Absence seizures</li>
<li>Tonic-clonic seizures</li>
<li>Tonic seizures</li>
<li>Atonic seizures</li>
<li>Myoclonic seizures (eg, in juvenile myoclonic epilepsy)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-partial-seizures">2. Partial seizures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-partial-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In partial seizures, the excess neuronal discharge occurs in one cerebral cortex, and most often results from structural abnormalities.</p>
<p>Partial seizures may evolve into a generalized seizure (called secondary generalization), which causes loss of consciousness. Secondary generalization occurs when a partial seizure spreads and activates the entire cerebrum bilaterally.</p>
<p>Partial seizures- sub divided into three types:</p>
<ul>
<li>Simple partial seizures</li>
<li>Complex partial seizures</li>
<li>Simple or complex seizures secondarily generalized</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-generalized-seizures">1. Generalized seizures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-generalized-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The seizure occurs without warning and consists of two distinct phases: <strong>Tonic</strong> and <strong>clonic</strong>;</p>
<p>In <strong>tonic</strong> phase the person rolls the eyes upward and immediately loses consciousness. If standing the child falls to the ground. The muscles stiffen in a generalized symmetric tonic contraction of the entire body. The arms usually flex, and the legs, head and neck extend and the mouth is shut tongue may be bitten, and this tonic phase may last for 10 to 30 seconds. The BP and the heart rate are increased and flushing and increased salivation</p>
<p>In <strong>clonic</strong> phase the tonic rigidity is replaced by intense jerking movements as the trunk and extremities undergo rhythmic contraction and relaxation, the child cannot control secretions at this time and may be incontinent of urine and feces. The average clonic phase lasts 30 to 50 seconds</p>
<p>In post ictal phase the child may remain semiconscious and difficult to arouse. The average duration of the postictal phase is from 1 to 15 minutes</p>
<p>Absence seizures- They have a sudden onset and are characterized by a brief loss of consciousness, a blank stare and automatisms</p>
<p>Atonic seizures- are manifested as a sudden, momentary loss of muscle tone</p>
<p>Myclonic seizures- are characterized by sudden, brief contractions of a muscle or group of muscles</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-partial-seizures">2. Partial seizures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-partial-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Simple partial seizures: simple symptoms and no alteration of consciousness</li>
<li>Complex partial seizures: complex symptoms and impairment of conscious</li>
<li>Simple or complex seizures secondarily generalized: simple or complex partial seizures that evolve into generalized seizures, usually a tonic-clonic event.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other terms used in convulsive disorders include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Epilepsy: Epilepsy is a condition characterized by two or more unprovoked seizures and can be caused by a variety of pathologic process in the brain</li>
<li>Status epilepticus: is a continuous seizure that last more than 30 minutes or a series of seizures from which the child does not regain a premobid level of consciousness</li>
<li>Febrile Seizures: Febrile seizures are diagnosed in children &lt; 6 yr with body temperature &gt; 38°C and no previous afebrile seizures when no cause can be identified and no underlying developmental or neurologic problem exists.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical evaluation</li>
<li>For new-onset seizures, neuroimaging, laboratory testing, and usually EEG</li>
<li>For known seizure disorders, usually anticonvulsant levels</li>
<li>For new-onset or known seizure disorders, other testing as clinically indicated</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Elimination of the cause if possible</li>
<li>Avoidance of or precautions during situations when loss of consciousness could be life threatening</li>
<li>Drugs to control seizures, which include diazepam, phenobarbitone, phenytoin sdium valporate</li>
<li>Surgery if ≥ 2 drugs in therapeutic doses do not control seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-seizures-and-status-epilepticus">Acute seizures and status epilepticus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-seizures-and-status-epilepticus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Most seizures stop spontaneously in several minutes or less and do not require emergency drug treatment. However, status epilepticus and most seizures lasting &gt; 5 min require drugs to terminate the seizures, with monitoring of respiratory status. Endotracheal intubation is necessary if there is any indication of airway compromise.</li>
<li>The sooner anticonvulsant therapy is started; the better and the more easily seizures are controlled.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poisoning-in-children">Poisoning in children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning-in-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Poisoning can be accidental in young children or suicidal in older children.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-principles-in-management-of-poisoning">General principles in management of poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-principles-in-management-of-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Supportive</p>
<p>Activated charcoal for serious oral poisonings</p>
<p>Occasionally use of specific antidotes</p>
<p>Only rare use gastric lavage</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="initial-stabilization">Initial stabilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initial-stabilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Maintain airway, breathing and circulation</p>
<p>IV fluids and sometimes vasopressors</p>
<p>56</p>
<p>IV dextrose to children with altered conscious level
IV naloxone should be tried on patients with apnea
IV thiamine should be given with or before to people suspected of thiamine deficiency e.g alcoholics, undernourished patients
IV fluids for hypotension</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topical-decontamination">Topical decontamination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topical-decontamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any body surface (including the eyes) exposed to the toxin is flushed with large amounts of water or saline, contaminated clothing, including shoes, and even jewelry should be removed</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="activated-charcoal">Activated charcoal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activated-charcoal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gastric emptying- should not be done routinely since it does reduce the overall morbidity and mortality
Whole bowel irrigation- can be used in some serious poisoning like heavy metals and drugs packets e.g. heroin and cocaine
Dialysis e.g. salicylate poisoning, theophylline
Specific antidotes
Supportive measures for hypoglycaemia, coma, and cerebral oedema
Seizures- anticonvulsant
Hyperthermia- cooling measures</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clearly labeling house hold products and prescription drugs
Storing drugs and toxins in cabinets that are locked and inaccessible to children to children
Promptly disposing of expired drugs
Use of carbon monoxide detectors
Use safety caps and containers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acetaminophen-poisoning-paracetamol">Acetaminophen poisoning (paracetamol)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acetaminophen-poisoning-paracetamol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acetaminophen poisoning can cause gastroenteritis within hours and hepatotoxicity 1 to 3 days after ingestion. Severity of hepatotoxicity after a single acute overdose is predicted by serum acetaminophen levels.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-and-signs">Symptoms and Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-and-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anorexia, nausea, vomiting and right upper quadrant abdominal pain, renal failure and pancreatitis may occur. Later -Hepatic involvement causes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Jaundice</li>
<li>Confusion</li>
<li>Stupor</li>
<li>Coagulation abnormalities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Serum acetaminophen levels are elevated</li>
<li>Rumack-Matthew nomogram</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral or IV N-acetylcysteine to prevent or minimize hepatotoxicity.</li>
<li>Possibly activated charcoal
Activated charcoal may be given if acetaminophen is likely to still remain in the GI tract.</li>
</ul>
<p>57</p>
<p>Carbon Monoxide Poisoning</p>
<p>Carbon monoxide (CO) poisoning causes acute symptoms such as headache, nausea, weakness, angina, dyspnea, loss of consciousness, seizures, and coma. Neuropsychiatric symptoms may develop weeks later. Diagnosis is by carboxyhemoglobin levels and ABGs, including measured O₂ saturation. Treatment is with supplemental O₂. Prevention is often possible with household CO detectors.</p>
<p>Aspirin and Other Salicylate Poisoning</p>
<p>After ingestion, acetylsalicylic acid (ASA) is converted to salicylic acid, its active form. Salicylic acid is absorbed in stomach and small intestines. Salicylate poisoning can cause vomiting, tinnitus, confusion, hyperthermia, respiratory alkalosis, metabolic acidosis, and multiple organ failure. Diagnosis is clinical, supplemented by measurement of the anion gap, ABGs, and serum salicylate levels. Treatment is with activated charcoal and alkaline diuresis or hemodialysis.</p>
<p>Organophosphate Poisoning and Carbamate Poisoning</p>
<p>Organophosphates and carbamates are common insecticides that inhibit cholinesterase activity, causing acute muscarinic manifestations (eg, salivation, lacrimation, urination, diarrhea, emesis, bronchorrhea, bronchospasm, bradycardia, miosis) and some nicotinic symptoms, including muscle fasciculations and weakness. Neuropathy can develop days to weeks after exposure.</p>
<p>Pathophysiology</p>
<p>Organophosphates and carbamates are absorbed through the GI tract, lungs, and skin. They inhibit plasma and RBC cholinesterase, preventing breakdown of acetylcholine, which then accumulates in synapses. Carbamates are cleared spontaneously within about 48 h after exposure. Organophosphates, however, can irreversibly bind to cholinesterase.</p>
<p>Diagnosis is clinical and sometimes with a trial of atropine, measurement of RBC acetylcholinesterase level, or both.</p>
<p>Treatment</p>
<p>Bronchorrhea and bronchospasm are treated with titrated high-dose atropine. Neuromuscular toxicity is treated with IV pralidoxime.</p>
<p>Key Points</p>
<ul>
<li>Organophosphates have been used in insecticides, medical treatments, and biologic weapons.</li>
<li>Suspect toxicity if patients have a muscarinic cholinergic toxidrome with prominent respiratory and neuromuscular findings.</li>
<li>Confirm the diagnosis by the response to atropine and sometimes RBC cholinesterase levels.</li>
<li>Treat supportively by giving atropine to relieve bronchospasm and bronchorrhea and by giving 2-PAM to relieve neuromuscular symptoms.</li>
</ul>
<p>58</p>
<p>59</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hydrocarbons">Hydrocarbons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydrocarbons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Examples of hydrocarbons include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Gasoline</li>
<li>Kerosene</li>
<li>Turpentine</li>
<li>Paint thinner and remover</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Gagging, choking and coughing</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
<li>Lethargy</li>
<li>Weakness</li>
<li>Respiratory symptoms of pulmonary involvement</li>
<li>Tacypnoea</li>
<li>Cyanosis,</li>
<li>Retractions</li>
<li>Grunting</li>
</ul>
<p>Immediate danger is aspiration (even small amounts) can cause bronchitis and chemical pneumonia; Gasoline, kerosene, lighter fluid and turpentine cause severe pneumonia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Inducing emesis is generally contraindicated. Gastric decontamination are questionable even when the hydrocarbons contain a heavy metal or pesticide, if gastric lavage must be performed, a cuffed endotracheal tube should be in place before lavage because of a high risk of aspiration. Symptomatic treatment of chemical pneumonia includes high humidity oxygen, hydration and antibiotics for secondary infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lead-poisoning">Lead Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lead-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(Plumbism)</p>
<p>Lead poisoning often causes minimal symptoms at first but can cause acute encephalopathy or irreversible organ damage, commonly resulting in cognitive deficits in children.</p>
<p>Diagnosis is by whole blood lead level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Treatment involves stopping lead exposure and sometimes using chelation therapy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="paediatric-hiv">Paediatric HIV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paediatric-hiv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>HIV stands for human immunodeficiency virus</p>
<p>AIDS stands for acquired immunodeficiency syndrome</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-clinical-staging-of-hiv-infection-in-infants-and-children">WHO Clinical Staging of HIV Infection in Infants and Children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-clinical-staging-of-hiv-infection-in-infants-and-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Stage I</p>
<ul>
<li>Asymptomatic</li>
<li>Persistent generalized lymphadenopathy (PGL)</li>
<li>Unexplained, asymptomatic Hepatosplenomegaly</li>
</ul>
<p>Stage II</p>
<ul>
<li>Papular pruritic eruptions (PPE)</li>
<li>Seborrheic dermatitis</li>
<li>Fungal nail infections</li>
<li>Angular cheilitis</li>
<li>Linear gingival erythema</li>
<li>Extensive HPV or molluscum infection (&gt;5% of body area/face)</li>
<li>Recurrent oral ulcerations (&gt;2 episodes/ in 6 months)</li>
<li>Parotid enlargement</li>
<li>Herpes zoster (&gt;1 episode/12 months)</li>
<li>Recurrent or chronic upper respiratory infection (URI): otitis media, otorrhoea, sinusitis (&gt;2 episodes/6 months)</li>
</ul>
<p>Stage III</p>
<ul>
<li>Unexplained moderate malnutrition (-2SD or Z score) not responding to standard therapy</li>
<li>Unexplained persistent diarrhoea (&gt;14 days)</li>
<li>Unexplained persistent fever (intermittent or constant, &gt; 1 mo.)</li>
<li>Oral candidiasis (outside neonatal period)</li>
<li>Oral hairy Leucoplakia</li>
<li>Pulmonary tuberculosis</li>
<li>Severe recurrent presumed bacterial pneumonia (&gt;2 episodes/12 months)</li>
<li>Acute necrotizing ulcerative gingivitis/ periodontitis</li>
<li>Lymphoid interstitial pneumonitis (LIP)</li>
<li>Unexplained anaemia (&lt;8g/dL), neutropenia (&lt;1000/mm3), or thrombocytopenia (&lt;30,000/mm3) for &gt;1 mo.</li>
<li>HIV-related cardiomyopathy</li>
<li>HIV-related nephropathy</li>
</ul>
<p>Stage IV</p>
<ul>
<li>Unexplained severe wasting or severe malnutrition (-3 SD or Z score) not responding to standard therapy</li>
<li>Pneumocystis pneumonia</li>
<li>Recurrent severe bacterial infections (&gt;2 episodes/12 months, excluding pneumonia)</li>
<li>Chronic orolabial or cutaneous HSV (lasting &gt; 1 mo)</li>
<li>Extra-pulmonary tuberculosis</li>
<li>Kaposi’s sarcoma</li>
<li>Oesophageal candidiasis</li>
<li>CNS toxoplasmosis</li>
<li>Cryptococcal meningitis</li>
<li>Any disseminated endemic mycosis</li>
<li>Cryptosporidiosis or Isosporiasis (with diarrhoea &gt; 1 month)</li>
<li>CMV infection of organ other than liver, spleen, lymph nodes (and onset age &gt;1 month)</li>
<li>Disseminated mycobacterial disease other than tuberculosis</li>
<li>Candida of trachea, bronchi or lungs</li>
<li>Acquired recto-vesicular fistula</li>
<li>Cerebral or B-cell non-Hodgkin’s lymphoma</li>
<li>Progressive multifocal leucoencephalopathy (PML)</li>
<li>HIV encephalopathy</li>
</ul>
<p>60</p>
<p>61</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="birth-testing-and-early-infant-diagnosis">Birth Testing and Early Infant Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#birth-testing-and-early-infant-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="birth-testing">Birth Testing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#birth-testing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Birth testing is defined as HIV testing (with DNA PCR) at birth or first contact within 2 weeks after birth, for infants born to known HIV-positive mothers.</p>
<p><strong>HIV DNA PCR testing should be done at birth or first contact thereafter within two weeks of birth for infants born to HIV positive mothers</strong></p>
<p>Birth testing has the potential to greatly improve survival for infants who are infected during pregnancy and around labour and delivery by identifying them early for rapid ART initiation.</p>
<p>For birth testing to be effective, facilities and programmes must provide the necessary resources, capacity, and infrastructure for optimum function of EID (early infant diagnosis) with a turn-around-time of ≤ 7 days for infant DBS PCR results.</p>
<p>Where capacity is limited to provide birth testing for all new-borns, it should be prioritized for the following infants at highest risk of antenatal HIV infection:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother has been on ART for &lt; 6 months</li>
<li>Mother’s most recent viral load (VL) before delivery was ≥ 1,000 copies/mL</li>
<li>No maternal VL available within the past 6 months</li>
<li>Mother known or suspected to be failing current ART regimen</li>
<li>Pre-term infants</li>
<li>Low birth-weight infants</li>
</ul>
<p>A new-born with a negative HIV DNA PCR at birth (or within 2 weeks of birth) should continue infant ARV prophylaxis and be followed as an HEI (HIV exposed infant). A repeat HIV DNA PCR test should be performed at 6 weeks and subsequent testing as recommended for all HEIs, following the EID (early infant diagnosis) algorithm</p>
<p>A new-born with a positive HIV DNA PCR is presumed to be HIV positive and should be started on ART immediately. A confirmatory HIV DNA PCR and baseline viral load should be taken at the time of initiating ART (initiation of ART is based on the first result). A positive 2nd PCR test confirms HIV infection; continue ART and routine follow-up as for HIV-positive infants. If the 2nd PCR is negative, these are discordant results: the infant should continue ART and send a 3rdDBS sample to NHRL (National HIV referral laboratory) to confirm HIV status.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="age-counseling-approach">Age Counseling Approach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#age-counseling-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>&lt; 6 years old - The counseling sessions will focus on engaging all of the child’s caregivers</p>
<p>6-12 years old</p>
<p>Both the caregiver and the child will be involved. The counseling will focus on the caregiver; younger children can be given a paper and pen and asked to draw their family, school, etc, and talk about their experiences.</p>
<p>Disclosure of HIV status to the child should commence by 5 years of age and be completed by 10-12 years of age</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="package-of-hiv-testing-services">Package of HIV Testing Services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#package-of-hiv-testing-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>An HIV testing and counselling session consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>A pre-test session</li>
<li>HIV test</li>
<li>A post-test session</li>
<li>Assessment for other health-related conditions or needs</li>
<li>Referral and linkage to other appropriate health services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary-of-hiv-testing-services-package">Summary of HIV Testing Services Package<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary-of-hiv-testing-services-package" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pre-test counselling/Pre-test information</p>
<p>Client-initiated HT (CITC)</p>
<ul>
<li>Introduction and orientation to session</li>
<li>Risk assessment</li>
<li>Consent for the test</li>
</ul>
<p>Provider Initiated HT (PITC) in health facility setting</p>
<ul>
<li>Introduction and information on importance of testing for HIV</li>
<li>Consent for the test</li>
<li>Test preparation</li>
</ul>
<p>Perform test using approved rapid HIV antibody test kit</p>
<p>Post-test counselling for negative results</p>
<ul>
<li>Risk reduction plan</li>
<li>Linkage to other HIV prevention services</li>
<li>Re-testing where applicable</li>
</ul>
<p>Post-test counselling for positive results</p>
<ul>
<li>Enrolment into comprehensive care and treatment</li>
<li>Risk reduction and positive living counselling</li>
<li>Partner/family testing</li>
</ul>
<p>Management</p>
<p>PMTCT Nevirapine Prophylaxis:</p>
<p>Age and dosing</p>
<p>0 - 6 wks- give Nevirapine dose- 10 mg (1ml) once daily (Birth weight &lt; 2,500 grams)
15 mg (1.5ml) once daily (Birth weight &gt; 2,500 grams)</p>
<p>6 - 14 wks give 20 mg (2mls) once daily</p>
<p>14 wks - 6 months give 25 mg (2.5mls) once daily</p>
<p>6 - 9 months give 30 mg (3mls) once daily</p>
<p>Duration of infant ARV prophylaxis: Immediately initiate Nevirapine (NVP) prophylaxis for 12 weeks</p>
<ul>
<li>Do HIV PCR test in accordance with national recommendations on early infant diagnosis;</li>
<li>Initiate treatment if the infant is Infected Infant identified as HIV exposed after birth (through infant or maternal HIV antibody testing) and is breastfeeding Nevirapine Immediately initiate NVP prophylaxis</li>
<li>Do HIV PCR test in accordance with national recommendations on early infant diagnosis</li>
<li>If results positive, initiate ART and stop NVP prophylaxis</li>
<li>If results negative, continue NVP prophylaxis up to 12 weeks</li>
</ul>
<p>Infant identified as HIV exposed after birth (through infant or maternal HIV antibody testing) and is not breastfeeding/on replacement feeding- give no drug and Do HIV PCR test in accordance with national recommendations on early infant diagnosis;</p>
<ul>
<li>No infant ARV prophylaxis;</li>
<li>Initiate treatment if the infant is infected</li>
</ul>
<p>Ongoing treatment/feeding</p>
<ol>
<li>If breast fed encourage exclusive breast feeding until 6 months. If an alternative to breast feeding is affordable, feasible, accessible, safe and sustainable (AFASS) discuss this option before delivery.</li>
<li>Do not abruptly stop breast feeding at 6 months, just add complementary feeds and continue nevirapine until 1 week after breast feeding stops.</li>
<li>Refer child and carers to an HIV support clinic.</li>
</ol>
<p>62</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>All HIV exposed / infected infants should start CTX prophylaxis from age 6 wks.</li>
</ol>
<p>Infants and children depend on their caregivers for adherence to medication. Palatability can also occasionally cause children to refuse medication. Caregivers should be adequately prepared for the role of administering ARVs to infants and children, including anticipated challenges and possible solutions.</p>
<p>&lt; 2 weeks AZT + 3TC + NVP3</p>
<p>2 weeks - &lt; 4 weeks ABC + 3TC + LPV/r</p>
<p>4 weeks - &lt; 3 years ABC + 3TC + LPV/r4</p>
<p>3 - 15 years (&lt; 35 kg body weight) ABC + 3TC + EFV5</p>
<p>3 - 15 years (≥ 35 kg body weight)</p>
<p>TDF + 3TC + EFV</p>
<p>&gt; 15 years TDF + 3TC + EFV6,7</p>
<p>PWID &gt; 15 years TDF + 3TC + ATV/r</p>
<p>Oral pre-exposure prophylaxis (PrEP)</p>
<p>Infant ARV prophylaxis is niverapine</p>
<p>Read;</p>
<ul>
<li>Disorders of the special senses includes conditions of the ear, nose, throat and eyes</li>
<li>Infectious diseases which include the communicable disease and diseases under immunization coverage</li>
</ul>
